O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, dearest son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine and its fulfillment. I have finished it with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And there came to me in a vision that I should complete this book with the treatise on surgery, which is part of the work of hands.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	For the work of hands is greatly neglected in our region and has been destroyed everywhere, so that its knowledge has perished and diminished, and there remains nothing of it but small descriptions in books which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed and the knowledge is obscured.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I wish to revive this knowledge along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation. And I will include alongside the forms of the instruments of cautery and other tools of the work with their declaration and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And whoever engages in this must climb into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the joints of limbs and their shapes and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, the number of openings, and the movement and rest of veins, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, but with a deed it is little; and this applies especially to the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things said before should guard against falling into error and killing people, as I have often seen many who engage in this science but abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who incised an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries in her neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another surgeon who drew a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to draw it out, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well whether cutting into him would cause his death.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And another surgeon took in charge the Duke of our land who had a broken leg with a wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, held the break on top of the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave any linen on the wound, leaving it thus at the end; and commanded that he should not untie it; and so it remained until the leg was entirely swollen and the foot rotted.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to go untie his leg; and when I heard it crackled so, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all paths of corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the whole member was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And another physician appeared who opened the enchanted abscess, and then inflamed it through the evil of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is purified of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all corrupted matter can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, surgery where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore you should be careful lest foolish physicians speak evil of you. Take up your implements with caution and undertake your patients lightly and steadfastly, using the best means so that through the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; leave frightful diseases requiring difficult treatment; put aside your implements concerning things that cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his teachings: 'Do not take on the care of a serious illness unless you are called a foolish physician.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, arranged from head to foot; and about the forms of instruments, iron tools for cauterization, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, cupping glasses, wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things; arranged from head to foot with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, I must describe the quality of the helper and the harm caused by each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the helper and of harm are the longest speech and subtle science and secret responses. And about this most of the wise spoke, and they agreed on it. They allowed me few words because I feared lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely, the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the temperament hot and dry together with matter, some said that cautery is great help there, but others said the opposite: that cautery is not useful for diseases coming from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat hot diseases with heat or dryness. And he who says the opposite argues that cautery provides great help for hot and dry diseases found in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to these words.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found this out sometimes by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And indeed, no one should meddle with this outside of those who have tried it and know by long practice the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and accidents and the changing seasons; we fear nothing else, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians gathered together and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, my son, that the cautery with fire is one of the secrets of treatments, and has greater effectiveness than a cautery with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not affect any other member but the one that is burned, and it does no harm if one can help it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines spread from member to member, causing severe inflammation and illnesses. Fire, due to its intensity and good nature, does not harm unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And what I have found by experiment and the length of service and study that I have put into this art, is true. And therefore I excuse myself for the length of my words, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that lies hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it overcomes diseases of the body, as philosophers demonstrate; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be made, and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that occurs is alleviated by its help; especially if the cauteries are for necessary and urgent pains which cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish physicians do; for a disease healed by cautery has no relapse; and they say this; but it is not so, because cauteries are not medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and are worth more than medicines for their speed of action, virtue of their work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	It is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its strength; and are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little excess moisture, such as cauteries for toothache and similar things, and this kind of pain does not return.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are valuable after medicine, their intentions are mistaken, and cauteries are indeed the last resort of medicine because when we administer various treatments for any disease and they do not work, then we apply cauteries, and they are effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	So it is clear that cauteries are indeed the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries of gold are gentler than those of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its nobility; but they said that the place of cautery does not cause rottenness, but this is not true as I have experienced it, and I found that in some people it does cause rottenness; and cauteries of gold are gentler than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat gold instruments, do not judge their heat by the color of the gold, for it quickly cools; and if they are heated too much, they become like fire; thus there is considerable hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from head to toe so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two kinds that are made due to a disease called 'soda,' and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears. It is also useful for a multitude of dreams, toothache, sore throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine softening the head for three nights or four, according to what the virtue and age and habit of the patient can tolerate; and then perform the procedure behind the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit crossed-legged between your hands, and place his hands on some weight; afterwards place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come together, there use the cautery called 'olivare', of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot, and move downwards and outwards with your hand little by little in a twisting motion; then raise your hand gently, and examine the spot if you see bone there; and if not, resume the cautery until you see bone as I told you; afterwards take a bit of wax, and put it inside soft cotton, and place it on the spot, leaving it for three days; afterwards place clean lint soaked in butter over it; leave it on until the burn is healed; then treat the wound with ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon' until it is sound.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as was said by the ancients, when a wound remains open for longer, it purges more; therefore, they recommended movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these say that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on until it penetrates as deeply into the bone as a skewer used by women for sewing, so that the humors may flow out more freely; and then one should let the wound remain open for a long time; afterwards, one should dress and bandage it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every case, except perhaps for some people who have cause for fear; and it seems better to me that I should leave the head alone; because the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and likewise when the patient's head is naturally weak, the first method of cautery seems safer and milder to me, and this is the one I now use most often.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When pain comes to the whole head chronically and lasts for a long time, then the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie," and cleansing of the head with oils and plasters; and if the cautery we mentioned earlier is performed on them, it will not be beneficial.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be cautious if the patient's head is of strong nature and is not too cold; then cauterize it with a little bit less of the cautery we mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, perform the cautery on the spot called "vassels"; and this is where cupping glasses are placed. Lightly touch your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries on the horns must be more subtle than those used for cauterizing the middle of the head, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and extends to the eye, and the head is purged with moisturizing medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned in the division of diseases are performed but do not help: then make cauteries in two ways, namely with medicine fire and hot iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with medicine fire is done thus: take an onion, remove its skin and crush it into two parts on the heads, then make a cut in the temple where the pain is felt so that you can place the onion under the skin; and when it is placed, tie it tightly and leave it like this for twelve hours; then untie it and remove the onion, leaving the wound like this for two or three days; then put on a cloth moistened in butter until it falls off.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed, and if you see fit to use some burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which there is a mold here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called a 'claw' because the head is shaped like a claw with a slight curve and a small point in the middle; and place it on the painful spot, holding your hand steady while turning the iron lightly until half of the width of the heart has been burned; then lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is behind, and there will be an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, put cotton soaked in water on the spot for three days; then put cotton moistened with butter and afterwards treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cautery called 'cutter', use only its point, taking care not to touch the artery in this wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	Of migraines
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraines as we have previously discussed in the division of illnesses, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries mentioned earlier in medicine do not benefit them at all, then you must heat the cautery called "cauterium" until it is white; and place it thus on the painful spot along a line half the length of two fingers, and once remove your hand so as not to cut the artery too deeply and reach the bone; and beware of the mandible that moves when chewing, and let the nerve only touch the muscle and prevent spasm from coming upon the patient, and beware of blood flowing from the artery when it is cut, or else have great fear especially if you are not skilled and experienced in this; and leave the work half done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals. And if you see [this], administer the cautery that we spoke of in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cautery having two blades; this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	due to pain in the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and one has opened it with dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in this section, but the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery called 'the point,' of which here is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After branding all around the sick ear, or all around both ears if the pain is in both, and moving away a little from the root of the ear after you have marked the spot to incise; and let there be ten points around each ear; afterwards treat the spot until it heals.
de la torture de la bouche	Of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	This torture that must be cured by fire cautery occurs only in those that move due to phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases. Do not perform cautery on similar conditions caused by heat and inflammation of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this condition of torture that moves due to phlegm with remedies such as hydrides and purgations of the head and gargling, if it does not help, then you must perform three cauteries on the patient: one at the root of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips. Place the cautery on the healthy part that is exposed, and apply the cautery above the head of the ear slightly below the horns, and another on the temple as long as a finger; leave the cautery until half of the wood is burned; this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the same applies to the scalpel we mentioned earlier, but it should be slightly finer and the blade somewhat thicker; afterwards, cure as I said before, until it is clean.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, but there is no improvement and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, one where it is called 'vessels', as we mentioned earlier, and one behind on the mouth of the stomach; and cure as we have said before.
de litargie	Of litharge:
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large drinks and pills that cleanse the brain. Afterwards, raise the head of the patient entirely, and place on the back of the head the plaster of mustard that is written about in the treatise on plasters; and this is the way to apply the cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed thus, it is good; and if not, apply three cauteries around the head descending to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery. And treat it like the others, and if you see it oozing, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, apply two more on the horns above, and treat until he is healed. And let the cautery be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and dirt as we have said before. Afterwards raise the patient's head, then apply cauteries around the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if more are needed, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, apply four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let them burn until the strongest of the heart is burned, then lift your hand. Afterwards treat until he is healed, and let the cautery be called "olivare" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should only use a fire cautery if they are phlegmatic. First one must modify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the previous division, when the patient is large and suffering from illness that requires medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, perform gargarisms and chewing remedies that modify the brain often with good foods. Afterward, raise the head in the middle, and perform the cautery as we have said before on the vessel and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, perform cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, using olive oil according to the method that I have mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When excessive moisture or corrupt humors are caused by melancholy and thick phlegm, then perform the cautery with hot irons as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities incline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something whereby the brain may be cleansed, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raising the patient's head; after make a compress of well-made linen, like a ring, and put it on the head; and the patient sits crossed-legged, and is held tightly from all sides; afterward present the compress, smeared with old sheep butter; and heat it gently over fire, so that the dough can suffer when it is placed on him; afterward remove the ring inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient each week once with other good governance, until he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you see cauterizing done by making many punctures all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery moistens the brain greatly; and then place on cotton dampened in butter and in goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the burning of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When burning comes first to the eyes with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something cleansing the head, and guarding against all moisture, and let them sweat or bathe many times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, instruct him to raise his head, and cauterize within the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of fire is on both eyes together, or one if it is on one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are below the heart with each cautery, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against bleeding, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stain it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of the cauter how to heal it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or scalpel below the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	Of the body's tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the forehead from outside, and it is seen that they are due to cold surplus moistures, then perform the cautery as described at the beginning of this chapter: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on each temple, and two cauteries behind the two cheekbones; and if more cauteries are needed, also cauterize the eyebrows above the eyebrows with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Of the body's tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in this division and there is no improvement, then give the patient three cow's droppings to drink at night. Afterward, raise his head, and perform a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery; and perform two cauteries with the cautery called 'clavilis' on both eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery so as not to cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called 'olivare'.
de coi ci est li forme:	This is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to make two cauteries on the two sides of the eyes as long as the eyebrows are; and do not let your hand rest there except until one-third of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	On the hair that points towards the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It sometimes happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned inward and point towards the eye, and cauteries are made upon them in two ways: namely, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient on your hand; afterwards, press a figure onto the paper over the eyes that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let it be placed at the beginning of the sign near the hairs; then put moistened cotton in egg white and coltsfoot powder onto the eye; then heat the cautery, which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing onto the figure that you have signed many times a little at a time until the skin is burned there; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs raised at the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days; then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is healed; afterwards, apply the ointment until it is sound.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs grow back and the paper is softened, then begin the cautery on that same place again as you did first; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery is what you should command the patient to let their hairs grow long and even. Then make parchment in the shape of a bay leaf; then take three parts each of French soap and live wax, grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then place it on the shape you have made like a bay leaf, and put it on paper over the eyes; and if the patient holds only one eye, operate on one, and if both, on both; and put moistened cotton under the eye in an egg shell; and let the head of the patient be in your hand and place your two fingers pointing at the medicine, and press the pouch and move it every time the patient feels burning from the medicine, for he feels burning like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the cauterization is complete, then lift the burning coal and observe if the paper lifts up as it would have been lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply the medicine again to the spot where the medicine did not act until your actions are even and your eyes steady; then place cotton dampened in butter so that the burning coal is extinguished. After that, cleanse the area with ointment called "diaphoresis" and others until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must take great care in your work so that no medicine gets into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes moist afterwards, and the hairs prick in the oil, then begin the medicine again on that spot softened by the paper properly, just as you did before. After that, cleanse it until it is clean; and this is the method of the cautery for warts.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this let your restraints be adjusted; and may not the straight way be replied to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then you must perform a cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your hand; and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or turn their head. Afterward, put moistened cotton on the eye or in a mixture of egg white or persillade juice. Then heat the cautery which is shaped like this: and raise it to the head as if it were the shape of a pigeon's feather, together with the cautery. If you see, point it from one end to the other, and if you see, make it like a tent; but in any case, that which is raised works better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, remove the corruption and dryness; and if it is closed, open it and bring forth the bowels; afterward place a hot cautery upon it, and keep your hand on the cautery at the part towards the nail above the eye, so that your hand does not act foolishly; and insert the cautery into the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and another time if necessary, leaving it for three days; afterward place cotton moistened in butter upon it, and continue the treatment with drying ointment until it is healed. And if forty days pass without it being healed, then apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is laid bare; and follow the rule according to what comes later in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of fistulary cautery which some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Make an incision for the fistula, and open up the location; afterwards place in the opening a thin stick like this which is shaped thus:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make of it the quantity of one third of an ounce; and hold your hand firmly on the stick so that the melted lead does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient moistened cotton in egg whites or in oil: the lead thus applied heals the fistula and the sore by wonderful healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to perform a trepanation on the nose and bring back the fistula to its proper place in the body.
des crevaices en levres	crevices in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Cracks in the lips, known as 'hair,' occur frequently, especially in children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fractures as we have described in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it immediately on these fractures until it reaches the bone; then clean the wound with wax until it is clear.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a boil comes at the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it causes decay and turns black and becomes filled with pus and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, but if it does not help: then you must take a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards burn or pierce the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and on the other side of the wound; and do this once or twice, after cleaning the wound as we have said in treatments, until it is clear; and if it is treated thus, that's good; but if not, then you must uncover the wound and remove the decayed bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of tooth movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but this does not work, then put the patient's head in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery whose shape will come later in this manner, so that you place a tube on the tooth; and put hot ashes into the cautery quickly, and hold your hand there until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards have the patient rinse their mouth with salted water, and keep it in for an hour and spit it out forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupting moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, either at the tooth or nearby, and remedies with medicine do not work, then there is need for a cautery in two ways: cautery of wax and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	**Cautery of butter is such that you take butter of cow's milk, and place the tip in an iron or brass spoon; afterward take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, then dip it into melted butter, and quickly put it on the aching tooth until it cools; and do this often so its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton become cold in the butter, put it on the aching tooth, and place it on hot iron until fire comes to the top of the tooth.**
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	**Cautery of fire together is such that you take an iron or brass rod, and let it be so thick that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; afterward heat the cautery, whose shape will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.**
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in haste during this cautery, and then hold the hot iron; this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform a cautery on whichever head you wish, according to what you can manage; and this is the form of the operation:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is full of phlegm and cold moisture, and does not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the hair cautery that follows this form, which has two openings for smoke to exit from the other side; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed until it reaches the bottom of the abscess. If the abscess is small, adjust the cautery according to its size and leave it on for three days. Then apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed. Afterward, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The forms of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moistures conquer the channels of the lungs, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient should first be made to vomit with soluble medicines; afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, but do not go too close to the throat, and burn only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then make another cautery at the junction of the neck and the top of the spine, using the kind called 'clavile' whose shape we have shown earlier; burn until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When cough and lung disease are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or shortness of breath, and the disease is chronic, then make two cauteries on the bladder in visible places; and another cautery between the two breasts; use the kind called 'clavile' according to the shape given earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make the fire cautery, pricking with the entire cautery called 'point', whose form is shown before in the disease of the ears; and let there be thirty or more points around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	And after treating the place according to what is said before, make three cauteries each of three grains in this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are easier to perform, since you make three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards have the patient lie on their back and side; then lift the heart which is inside the titillite with the backs of your left hand fingers; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery that has two grains to this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	Cauterize the heart until it pierces to the side, and bring together four figures of the cautery; thus, cauterize with the cautery that has three points, so that the forms of cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent, this is the form of the cautery that has three points.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is added onto this one nerve, thus there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Next, apply the cautery to the broken parts with a wick; then allow the patient to rest, and do not move the member for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then apply the cautery to the thick part of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For when the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach, drawing it away from its natural state, and catharsis increases in him, but he does not benefit from customary treatments, then the patient must be made to lie on his back, extending his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then make three cauteries under the armpit of the arm, using two fingers' quantity at each cautery, and two cauteries below the two ribs so that the figure of the cauteries forms a triangle with equal spacing between them to prevent merging when they ulcerate; and let the cauteries be deep enough to reach both parts of the heart, with the figure of the cauteries following this form precisely.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form, and whoever fears that cautery should cauterize by pricking and pressing upon the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize to the full extent of the cautery called "the point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we had before, once it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	If liver pain arises from coldness and moisture and excessive windiness, causing it to lose its natural complexion due to excesses; and despite the treatments we've mentioned in divisions, the patient finds no relief, then the patient should be bled on their left side; And there are three cauteries to be applied according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the ribs meet; And each cautery should have the width of two fingers between them; And the cauteries should be long, not pressing too hard with your hand throughout; And only half of the chest should be burned, and the patient should stand on their right foot; And if they cannot stand, then lie down, extend legs, and raise arms; This is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the cutter, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and ensure that you do not burn all the heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and let it not come near the eye, for the heart is very subtle there, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the skin: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too intense; and if it is in the skin, they feel fierce pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this treatment fails the doctors, it is necessary for the patient to be seated on their head; and then hold firmly the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that resembles a ray, of which there is the form below:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burned, and go as far as the sphincter, until the passage is entirely open; afterward, treat according to the treatment of the veins until it is healed; and only those who have studied medicine at length should use this cautery, through whose hands these diseases have cured many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he may boldly operate, yet still it seems to me that it is better to let them alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Regarding the cautery for the lungs
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries with the roots of aristologus (a type of plant), and in this manner: Take a root of aristologus as long as possible, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your two fingers; and soak it in oil, and take it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower down on the part that is under the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining somewhat behind; and one cautery in the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on either side of the breast away from the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly, just as you would with perfume.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients said that certain people used to use a fire cautery similar to a razor, heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and if pain occurs, as we have mentioned in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies suddenly, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse according to what we have said regarding its divisions and remedies, but it does not improve, then there are three kinds of cautery that can be used.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
