Of which the first manner is that you make three or four cauteries along the length of the mouse, following the figure of the liver cautery that we have mentioned earlier; and do not press your hand throughout the cautery, and let the patient lie constantly on their back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the heart that is near the mouse, where the ribs of the patient come towards the left, and let the elevation by which you raise the heart be according to the height of the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After this, insert the two burning irons so that the heart is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, thus having four in total. If you see fit, cauterize all of it with three irons.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After this treatment, if there has been putrefaction for a long time, it is better that the others mentioned before are done.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy unless it is done in the manner called "ascites.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then you must perform four cauteries around the belly button, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one near the navel, two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the breast; and let the cauteries be close to the edge of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to expel long-standing putrefaction and do not neglect the treatment of the patient after the cautery; then healing will hasten, with both intentions being together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is that which we have shown before; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what has been placed here.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet of someone who is dropsical are swollen and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and raise your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep, lest you break through the yellow water, and let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the shinbone; and let the cauteries be long, one in front below the knee and the other behind in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without dressing them until the water runs out; afterwards apply the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the dislocation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When a stomach ailment arises from coldness and moisture such that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by usual methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly despite their strength, then make a large cautery on the stomach as spoken of earlier regarding the stomach cautery, along with four subtle cauteries around the belly button like so many little nails, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moistures and the patient is suffering, make one cautery on the hip, and one on each thigh, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one; for the treatment is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as mentioned earlier but without benefit, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, the one directly opposite the nape of the neck and two below the navel; and if you think that the stomach is cooled and the flesh not cooked, and the face appears swollen, then make one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned earlier, another on the liver, and another on the mouse with each cautery like a little nail; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, heal the place until it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the fleshiness which is named "thelul", then heat up the cautery that seems like a razor, and then place it entirely ablaze upon that cut fleshiness; and let your hand remain there until the cautery reaches the beginning of the vein where blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there is much fleshiness, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards, heal with ointments useful for healing until it is sound; and if you cauterize with a large cautery upon fat fleshiness, it will have greater benefit.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its proper place, then comes such a disease that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When someone has a fistula and it is inflamed and filled with putrid matter and corrupt moisture, then you should probe it carefully throughout its entire length, ensuring that you know the full extent of its depth.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to how much the tent has entered. Then continue applying the cautery until those rotted and corrupted bodies are burned once or twice or three times depending on what is needed; be careful not to burn the nerves that are within and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula leads to the body of the bladder and the intestines, be careful at these locations and only perform cautery on thick flesh. Consider that it is not permeable; afterwards, treat the area until it is clean, and if the location is sealed and the matter has been removed for a long time, know that the location is entirely healed. And if the matter has not been removed, know that the location is damaged, and the bone at the front is rotted; thus one of these things will happen which we will discuss in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, and there is great windiness, and no desire for sexual intercourse, then you must perform a cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the clavicle cautery that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is cold and weak due to moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then perform a cautery on the lower part of the bladder where the pubic hairs begin, one on the right side and one on the left, each cautery being as long as a grain of wheat; and also perform one cautery behind the back if necessary; and let the cauteries be made with the clavicle cautery according to the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception because of it, and the flowers are corrupted and their periods delayed; and when they do come, there is great pain: then one must perform three cauteries around the navel as we have said for the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be made with the clavicle cautery as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hair
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When moist viscous humors descend to the bladder of the hair, and due to this it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh appears longer than the other when measured together; and the place of division is found empty, then you should cauterize the patient on the bladder of the hair with a cautery resembling a circle, and press before the place around the bladder as it turns, so that the bladder is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, then make three large olive-shaped ones, and let the cautery be as deep as all the hearts; and perform the cure until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hair
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the bladder of the hair, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is not cured by what we have said regarding division and the cure does not help, and the illness is chronic: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After this, perform cautery. There are two methods of cautery:
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is such that you apply three triangular cauteries according to this form on the scrotum, with good depth and width, keeping space between each cautery about the size of two fingers, and let them be olive-shaped. Sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the scrotum, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, apply the cautery at the cautery of the circle that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the scrotum; but do it in such a manner that the circle contains all the scrotum, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain resides in the scrotum and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, apply two cauteries where the patient feels the pain, and one cautery above the ankle on both sides slightly on the left; let the cauteries be shaped like a scalpel, and burn the thickness of the heart. And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers from the foot or near it, apply cauteries there three points or four at the point called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more is needed, then he should do it; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, he should make a cautery using the cutting cautery or circular cautery, and be sure in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and thus cause the patient greater harm and scarring.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it on so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted altogether.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the abdomen which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise say concerning the cautery of the groin: this is the manner to make it - let it be made of such iron that at its head it is as thick as a large hazelnut or somewhat less, and let it be perforated with holes evenly spaced, each hole being as wide as the thickness of a goose quill; and let the holes be rounded on both sides like nuts, and let there be one well-made handle for it. This is its shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	**And let it be heated until it is completely red and glowing hot, and then place it on the box of the sick person's hair, turned towards their sound side; and cauterize once with fire, the cautery should remain for three days; and then make an emplaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.**
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	**Albucasis says that we do not use this cautery much because of its fearsome appearance, and we see few who employ it; nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured where it affects.**
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	**The burning cautery is such that you make one instrument with intersecting parts in which the edges of the door slide down, and it should be made of brass or iron on one long side, two fingers high at the top, each with the quantity of the thickness of a finger between them; and they should be open at the front and above, joining together in this form:**
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the box of the herb on the patient lying on their healthy side, press your hand firmly onto the box of the herb; then place between the two circles of the hot awl that has been heated in the fire for one hour, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning sensation.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there will be a biting sensation like fire; and when the biting sensation has passed, remove your hand with the instrument and lift the hot herb compress, leaving it for three days. Then apply butter until the blackened area is gone; leave for another three days to draw out corruption. This would be the final assistance after treating with ointments once it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, make one instrument similarly for the awl as you did for the herb compress. This is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and live coals, an equal amount of each, grind them together, and place them in nine pots.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	On which there is a small hole made such that the point of a razor can enter; and put another well-sealed pot on top of this pot, then place some sweet-tasting water on top of the quicklime and live coals, until you have about two handfuls of the powder mixed with water. Leave it like this until water drips into the sealed pot below, then take all that water and pour it onto the quicklime and live coals as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very hot and effective for many medical purposes and fire cauteries of other limbs. For it performs the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hair well, such as mustard and honey mixed with walnuts and soap mixed with live coals; all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where a man was healed from the pain of sciatica and thigh vein, and he praised it greatly, saying that no other cure was needed, and that he was completely cured in one session after this cure was performed, as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner: that you take some fresh and dry green verdigris, grind it much with a little fat, apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is felt, let it lie; leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then make him enter a bath until his body is slightly aroused, then have him lie in bed, and the pain will all go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery with such medications except after an evacuation of flesh.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be performed in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take flaxseed, heat it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the one called the fleshy bump.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Next, take dry goat dung and heat it over fire until it turns to charcoal. Place it on the flaxseed and let it sit until it is cooked. Repeat this process again and continue until you believe by sense that it reaches the hip joint and the pain ceases; this method of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	for back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back due to falling or from blunt force trauma or from excessive bleeding, or from similar causes of cold matter dispersed throughout, cauterization is not beneficial except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been relieved of fetid pills or similar remedies applied to their back where the pain is located, make three lines of marks with a hot iron branding tool, each line five inches long. In each line, apply between five and more cauteries depending on the strength and amount that the patient can withstand; use the cautery method known as "poins" for this procedure. If you see fit, perform three or four cauteries using the midpoint clavicle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the sign of its beginning is that they have a tight back when they rise up, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance which rises above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to treat it, cauterize it with a hot iron according to this method.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three lines apart, and let the points be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treatment, ensure the area is clean according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply a hot iron to any gibbosity near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are due to moistures that have spread throughout each limb of the body, and when pain comes on in the feet, which doctors properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, it is treated by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the ankle joint, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	If it is necessary for you to press upon the sole of the foot, then perform the cautery at all the cauterizing points that are called 'points'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If the pains extend to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then perform three or four cauteries on each knee at all the olive-shaped cautery points; and if you need more, then perform more, but do not exceed the length of a fingerbreadth so that the 'heart's blade' is not burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	If the pains descend to the knee and back, then administer the cautery that we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	If the pains are in the hands, then make two punctures around the wrist; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, then make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains extend to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each area, and provide good care for the patient and give medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If thou dost govern him well and purge fleume, then shall he be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of removing the tonsils
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When tonsillitis occurs and the swollen glands descend to the chin, if it is recent, then when you see him for treatment, let him not eat that day; and let him use things that leave the belly empty, so that the phlegm descends from his belly. Afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and tell him to turn his head until the glands are repaired, and align them with your two fingers, and press firmly beneath the tonsil onto the bone of the chin, and keep a sign like half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery for which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white-hot and emits sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the glands to their place; and the assistant holds his hand so they do not go back; and open the patient's thighs well, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the thighs, and another under his chest which supports his hands. Then place the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and press with your right hand until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone. And be careful that the gland does not jump out while you are using the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and that the patient does not die from this, or suffer another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that cauteries for children be thin according to the measure of an egg, and those for large people be large according to their size; afterward on the third day treat the wound with butter until the blister is removed; afterward treat it with other ointments until it heals, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time so that his eyes do not bulge out when he tries to get up.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And afterward on the fortieth day, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage and keep it on for forty more days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much or guard against excessive drinking and eating, and loud laughing; and if he follows this teaching, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow larger, perform the cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and let the third of the heart be burned; afterwards treat according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the beginning of the incision and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another below it, and hold your hand in the middle during the entire cautery with a hot iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in some limb, either from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is worthless there, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called 'point', and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, that's good; but if not, apply another cautery on top of it, for it is customary for the skin to become accustomed to the nearby member, therefore you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of varicose veins
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Varices are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, especially those that come from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	But if you wish to cauterize the veins, be careful if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in our division, and does not recur or remain, but you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the patient; then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; two on the two horns [temples], and one behind on the back of the neck; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the skins come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize it on the muscle according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the melancholy is spread throughout, and it is apparent, then you should cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery near the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the ribcage and another beside it, and two on each shoulder, and two on the ribs, and two on the breasts' tendons, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the palms' hollows; and beware of the nerves that are above the heel bone, lest you burn them; and sometimes one cauterizes on the wrist bone, and another on the stomach's bone, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you perform, the more help you give, and the greater the benefit; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in various iron methods.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After applying flour of doves with honey and other remedies until it is clean.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but it is not healed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size and length; and let the cautery be a little deep into the flesh near the heart; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is applied to the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if the swelling has been removed; but nonetheless let no one meddle with it unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	I do not understand.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called 'albaras' is inflamed, and the power of medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a cautery that is somewhat deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the heart; until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with flour of doves and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of crow and blood of pigeon, each one part; and let everything be mixed together, and let it be tied with a cloth, and let it be applied to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stopped, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And moreover, the wise said that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, which has happened on many occasions. And it is much more advisable that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called 'circule', as we have said regarding many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called 'adubelati', and it delays in healing because of the excessiveness that it causes, or due to the weakness of the patient when they are elderly (that is, too old) and they have a lack of blood, or because of the time; if you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries, pressing; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced by all the cautery, then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels faint in such a way that the course of the corruption is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cautery by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than the consumption of a limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate a fire cautery, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what is needed for the location where the disease is; afterwards, cauterize it on all sides until you have burned away all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it rest for 3 days, applying heated poultices with oil until the burns and all corruption are gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of inflammation-causing ointments.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days you see that healthy flesh does not grow, then it is good; and if not, recommence the cautery on that which remains of the corrupted skin.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this wound has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already described the cure for hot medicine in its place. Take however much you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pores that come at the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often at the feet by default arises an illness called 'clot' according to our understanding, which is a large broken thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this illness is in two ways:
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery of fire is that you heat the cautery iron as hot as a smith's pencil, and let it be made of good iron to the measure that it can encompass the nail on all sides, and that there are subtle edges; after this, put it all hot onto the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to throw off rottenness; then make a poultice of wild mallows ground with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place with ointment that is warming and good until it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they turn away from the body, and this happens many times in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery of hot water to them; and it is done in this way: take a tube of brass or iron, or a smith's pencil, and put it on the nail and its attachments, that is to say warts; and put the tube on so that it encompasses all around, then put some hot water into it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the nail, and can find a deep path for the hot water to reach the root; and let the patient suffer the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot itself completely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus one does after another, until you extract all those that are in the body, then dress them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	to treat trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of nerves or quartan fever or other cause, then you must perform four cauteries on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot and one above the stomach at the solar plexus; then trembling will cease, and recovery from the cold illness will be hastened.
des pustules puans	of foul boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the body Baths or foul boils which come from large corrupted matters
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	then it is necessary at first when they appear to perform cautery on each head of the boil: one fine cautery made from myrtle wood with its point heated in fire or a long root of aristolochia or a lenticular cautery
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes cauterization is applied at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further thereafter, but the excess from which they come is broken off, and they are clean; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is very painful to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to someone, quickly place your two index fingers on the wound of the vein and press hard until the blood is calmed beneath your fingers and no longer flows out; then put into the fire olive oil cauteries both small and large until they are all red; then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is severed, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if sparks fly when you lift your finger off the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another from those in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is completely extinguished; and beware that you do not burn the nerve nearby, nor bring any other harm upon the patient. And know that when blood spurts from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped unless through one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is untreated, or by strongly tying a thread, or by applying medications with the power to stop bleeding; and let it be tied and tightly bound appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Those who bring about stopping of blood through the narrow tying of bandages or placing burning things on it, or similar methods, will profit little if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no doctor or medicine present, then place your index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding over the wound and the vein. Do not move your finger, but moisten it with cold water frequently, ensuring that it is very cold until the blood congeals, thickens, and stops flowing. Then afterwards do what is necessary regarding cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases for which a fire cautery or hot medicine is needed, as well as their causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from head to toe, and I will follow the same path in this chapter so that one may more easily find what one seeks.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this one, dear friend, it is necessary for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauteries, and therefore greater care is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the practice of this chapter, there are many times evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I caution you not to attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Indeed, many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Yet some people become so attached to their illness that they die quickly due to the foolishness they find in their condition and the severity of their affliction; one should fear these individuals.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who seem to recover, saying: 'Wait, I am cured'; but the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you agree with those who come to you with such manner, but place greater care in your honor than in your greed. Do not open yourself foolishly to those from whom you can gain profit and fame, but use prognosis and indication in treating your patients so that they may be restored to health. This will help you achieve good reputation, glory, and the memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if it pleases Him to inspire you with His holy breath, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in sections, dividing it into chapters, following what is ahead of the chapter on cauteries which I have already divided from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Of the full head of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the womb squeezes the child's head too tightly; sometimes it is also caused by some unknown reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness except in children, and all those that I saw died quickly; and therefore it seems to me that it is not worthwhile for me to linger on such treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and it swelled each day until it could no longer bear it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture gathered beneath the bone above the fontanelle, between the heart and the bone. And if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you should cut a wide slit in the head; let it be as long as two fingers, until the moisture runs out. Here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If moisture is greater and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this pattern:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if moisture is under the bone, and you see signs that the angles of the head are raised on each side, and water flows out when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not respond: then you must make three incisions into the head according to this manner
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After closing the incisions with bandages and powders, apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then release it, and treat the wound with dressings and ointments, and keep the head wrapped evenly, and give the patient dry food made from pork broth until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe where the opening of the abscess appears, and how the water collects; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess opens, and draw out the water, and make the incision according to your ability; and be careful that you do not cut the artery; and let a vein flow with blood, so that the patient dies from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or nostrils, and the disease is chronic, and medicinal remedies do not help, then the final remedy is cauterization with the cutting of both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cut the veins, make sure that the patient turns their head back; then rub the spot with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient hold their head down with both hands on the cloth; then look where the vein runs and mark the places of both sides after the ears, then make incisions with a sharp spatula two parts wide until you reach bone, doing this on both sides of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, place the scalpel beneath the artery and cut above it, cutting as much as two should.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, blood flows out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at touch, then measure three finger widths of space, then press down and cut until it reaches the bone; as much blood as six drops should flow out, sometimes a bit more or less depending on what the patient can tolerate and the pressure in the artery. Then examine the wound: if there is still flesh on the bone tip, cut away any excess skin, then press the wound shut and bind it, applying ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of diarrhea
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic diarrhea and catarrh occur, due to moistness of tears and heat in the temples with accompanying old madness and similar ailments, and medicine does not help him at all, then extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient raises the hairs of his temples, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens clearly by its beating, and is little responded outside except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responded, then the patient holds its neck with some cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with warm water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatumile of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then carefully scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then raise it with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath it on each side; and if the artery is delicate, then cut it off at the point of a needle, then cauterize that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cauterized, then the blood will flow completely on all sides.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out six drops of blood from the wound, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong silk thread doubled, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and let there be a flow of blood; then cut off the superfluity that is between the two ties at that same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with the scalpel cautery up to the bone until the flesh is cut; and this is the proper work if the patient does not have fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is helpful in finishing off moistures: therefore it is more helpful for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on well-made bandages; and when they are untied, then cure them with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until they are healthy; and if without court of the artery as often as you work there, then hasten to cut by cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and press it with your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have this present, then put your fist on the place until the blood is congealed, and rinse the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and be pressed as it should; and what is quickest and easiest in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cutting cautery from two sides, but let the cuts be well-spaced to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the irons are too thin, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there must be a space of two fingers between the two knives, one thick and wide; then when you have marked with them both places, hold the glowing iron on each until it reaches the bone, cutting open the vein in both places; and let them be far apart between the two heads for this cautery is not wholly continuous all around; and that is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes flow down the veins that are above the brow of the forehead, and medication does not help, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feel a trembling on the forehead like shivers; and if both eyes are thin and moist so that the hairs of the eyebrows fall out, and the brows are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it 'cure contuse', and you should do this to the patient who has this disease: make three cuts on their forehead, evenly spaced according to its length. One of the cuts should be just like two fingers wide in the middle of the forehead going downwards towards the nose; the other two cuts should be placed on either side of the temples, and you must avoid cutting into the arteries that lie on either side of the temples. Keep your hand away from the continuation of both jawbones, and each cut should be about three fingers wide across. Then prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping off the blood, and then insert the spatumile through this opening.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And from the incision that starts at the temple going towards the second incision; then strip off all the skin that is between the two cuts as far up as it goes onto the bone, and then continue from the middle cut towards the other side cut, after which you should remove this spatumile.
