si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert into the first opening the tool called "cultellaire", which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other side, that is its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge of the tool towards the flesh near the heart, and the soft edge towards the bone, inserting it until it reaches the middle opening.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to those that open near the heart, and then similarly do in the middle opening up to the other side; then draw out the blood evenly, expressing the area for the taken blood. Then place in each opening a pad of old cotton, and put over it cloths moistened in wine and oil and rose water, ensuring no abscess forms. On the third day untie the dressing, and bring plenty of sage water, then use basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments to heal wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Concerning the treatment of eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh comes often and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakens vision, with burned papers; and hair falls out, and in deep pain at the head, and the patient sneezes. Then know by these symptoms that this matter and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure for it is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should command the patient to lie on their back, then make a great incision between the eyebrows, and another one from the eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let it be until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that move during chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then open between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen cloths; then tie above with rags moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot swelling; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying substances that cause skin to form.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to prevent flesh from rotting.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the bursting of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grain, or beast, or mining stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or fluid thing such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other manner of thing falls into the ear that does not fit in the ear nor grow within it, place the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then apply extraction; and when doing so cause sneezing with mustard powder, and hold his nostrils closed during sneezing, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and elevate the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Fire cautery is often necessary for this treatment; if it cannot be used, then use tweezers to extract it. Here is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it cannot be extracted with tweezers, then use a thin needle with a small double-edged blade; if that does not work, make a funnel of silver and insert its tip into the earhole firmly, then stuff the space around the funnel with soft wax so that wind cannot enter through the funnel. Then strike fire strongly, as it is often necessary to do so as we have said. If it still does not come out in this manner, take some bird glue, attach it to some instrument pointed for this purpose, wrap a bit of cotton around it, press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and strike fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it still does not come out despite all these methods we have mentioned, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess forms and causes inflammation or spasm. The method of cutting is as follows: first bleed the patient from the head according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small crescent-shaped incision at the root of the ear where it depends. Then pull out the stone according to your ability and suck it quickly into your mouth. Continue this treatment until the patient is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer an extraction; but if it cannot come out, then administer the tenacious thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many small incisions. Then extract it with fine tweezers and wax, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sternutation first, and then clean the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on their ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it drains out through this [incision], that's good
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	But if not, take many fine and light needles according to the length of your thumb, heat them slightly in fire; and have the patient put one into his ear hole, and let it come out on the other side. Then pierce another needle onto the one that is in the ear; and do this continuously until all the water drains out, and then let it drain out completely. If you see, take a reed and put one end into the ear, and heat the other end with fire until the tip of the reed catches fire. Then repeat this process with other reeds until all the water drains out, as we have said about needles.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of an animal, if it is small-bodied such as fleas and similar creatures, treat it as we have said in division. But if it is large bodied so that one can feel it, bring about extraction with pincers; this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of earthworms in ears, when treating it as we have said in division and where treating distillations, if the cure does not help at all, then you must examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms appear, remove them with fine pincers. If none are visible, take the tube described below:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Insert the finest tip into the ear according to the amount of suffering the patient endures, then suck strongly on the entire tube; do this repeatedly until all worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey in coming out, stuff cotton around the tube as I have said regarding stones. And if they still do not emerge as we have said, bring about distillations that the ancients have proven effective in expelling worms, which you will find in the section on treating distillations. And if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, here is its shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Whether it's made of silver or hard brass below with small holes, and above for distillation; and to press within the distillation use a well-made brass tool suited for this purpose. Then take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip carefully; then pour your oil or juice along with any medicines you wish into the funnel, placing the funnel in the ear. Next insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled out of the ear; let the patient feel it inside, and heat the distillation vessel over the fire before distilling it into the ear; ensure it's not too cold, as the medicine would not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of clearing the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; the same applies to adults due to injuries or flesh growing inside the ear. Sometimes these blockages go deep into the ear so they cannot be seen. And sometimes there is an absence of holes, which can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from deep within, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult cure in many cases. But that which can be seen, you must place your ear to the patient's sunken eye; look inside: if you see the clouding apparent, then know this is the form of all this spatumile of which here is the figure.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting both before and behind entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear. If the clouding is of flesh born in or on the body of the ear, then grasp it with fine tweezers, and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the clouding is deep within the ear, then take a fine razor lightly and heat it slightly on the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the clouding about which the patient complains of hearing, then pierce lightly, and take care not to harm the nerves of the ear. Then place in the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moist it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make sure some days that the wound is healed, or you take a cloth and wet it in rose water, and powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must draw out the cloth and move another cloth wetted in cerote made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is removed; then dress it until it's clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding starts, then plunge a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are found in treating distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of papyrus
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the preparation that comes from papyrus when they are moist and dry: you must stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off with a scalpel its roots; then put powdered vitriol on the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood comes out, then cauterize it with the lenticular cautery and the cautery after the incision should be moved; and often they repair, because some things remain from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Thunder
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, papers come from the eyes containing things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," which is a gathering of large moisture on top and below the paper. The treatment is: watch carefully if the hail moves from one side to another, and it's easy to know; then make an incision widely, then gently scrape each part, then take it with tweezers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	But if you cannot cut it without piercing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient. And if the split is large, then sew it up and heal it until it's healthy; but if it is small, do not exert force on it because the eyes will soon restore it naturally.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail descends into the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper and take the hail with tweezers, cut it and press it on both sides. And if the paper is torn away by the incision, it does not harm; and when the hail is cut, rinse the eye with saltwater and heal the wound until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is entrenched in the tissues of the eyelids above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, causing great discomfort to their eyes. It brings forth catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because tears quickly gather in their eyes; therefore, they constantly lie on their faces and sleep thus, with their eyelids moist underneath their eyebrows, giving the appearance of having exinach which opens into the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place between your two eyes and feel the exinach within
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of performing this operation is as follows: the patient places his head in your hand, and then you take a linen cloth and prepare it like a circle according to the amount of exinach contained on each side. Then place it on top; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle. Then make a small cut in the middle with a sharp scalpel, not larger than the incision made for phlebotomy, and cut deeply until you reach the exinach. In several positions, exinach will come out of the incision like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out then a whole piece of soft cloth between your two fingers and twist your hand to the right and left until it is scattered; and make sure you do not push into the crevice, so that you do not reach all the way up to the eye, so that you do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the crevice, then carefully widen the crevice a little until it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then wet cloths in warm and cold water, and place them on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who crush it and apply it to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess forms in its place, then treat it with soothing poultices until it heals.
des poilz des papieres	Hairs of the papyrus
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs are born on paper close to each other unlike those naturally found there, and they are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases like habitual tears and softening of the papers and cloudiness, leading to destruction of the eyes. The treatment is done in four ways: either by cauterizing with fire together or by applying an ointment as mentioned earlier in the chapter on cautery, and it can also be done through incision and stitching or through drops according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye with your left hand; if it turns correctly, that's good; but if not, insert a needle at the top of the thread on top. And this should be near the edge of the paper where the hairs are born close to these hairs, and pull the thread upwards across the entire paper, then turn it towards the razor. Then make an incision below the paper, below the closely-growing hairs, with the curved part of the scalpel from the large eyelid to the small one. Then remove the thread, and place a small cotton cloth and gauze underneath the paper. Next, press down on the paper with a mirror-like figure, like a mortar pestle, ensuring that the figure is according to the quantity you see raising the divided paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one has need to cut off a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make incisions on both sides along the two lines that you have marked, starting from the larger circle down to the smaller; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert it into one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape it all off; then join the two lips with a stitch using a single thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make dry the excess threads over the two eyebrows with any sticky substance you see fit to use; and if not, pay no heed, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting substances, because the paper livens at the union of the wound and its joining together, but stitches are mute (as the ancients said), and this is the work without fear; and there is another manner: it is that you mark the paper with a figure like the laurel leaf, as we have described, with three points equidistant according to the form given here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which exceed the small ones evenly according to the form shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; and place another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring together between your two fingers evenly; then raise your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have said, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms on your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment. And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: so you must use those we have said about incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canthi is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make an incision inside according to what I have said, and then make two canthi artificially, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; and cut at the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads; then bring together one and the other subtly on top of the paper of the eye, and tie the two canthi of the two parts firmly; and leave it like this for a few days, and the skin that is tied will die and shrivel and fall off until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, cut with some force, then heal it until it is clean; and when the wound has closed, and if the paper has been removed, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the shape of the two cauteries that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: take a fine needle and thread it with one strand of soft silk; then gather the ends and tie them both finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length. Then prepare another short strand of silk thread, and tie its ends to those of the other thread. Then have the patient place their head in your lap, and stand near the sun so that the operation is well lit, for this is a delicate and small procedure. Then insert the needle along the chase up to the root of the hair, and pierce it into the paper swiftly until you draw it out above the natural hair. Then pull out the hair up to the chase, and insert the hair thus if there is one or two or three or more. Then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out along the chase with the paper and the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the dart is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the dart from below along all the thread that you have ordered there, until the dart comes out through the hole above and you can see it with your eye; then pull out the dart and the thread, close the eye, and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days until the hair returns to its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are few, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it with that one which you leave, until it is lengthened and then lift it up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the rottenness of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called 'aleacrati' or rottenness comes to the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working it is that you break this joint, and separate the lips of it, and put linen cloths within, and keep it until it is healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	But if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it works with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or almond water and linseed should be cooked, and applications of diachylon melted in some oils, and a cloth is wrapped around it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must ensure that it does not heal in the same shape as before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are remedies for this disease so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called truly 'axacration' and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and split and cautery and similar things; and the way of doing it in this case is that you take a needle with doubled thread and insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left eyelid to the right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut with a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that's good; but if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, turn the paper, and make two splits on either side inside the paper; let the ends of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the figure is like the figure of a letter called "I Greek"; then remove that flesh according to how much its sides were attached beneath, from what supports the paper, then join the two separated parts with a thread of wool; then treat it with the remedies we have spoken of for softening medicines and dressings until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or a wound or a cautery burn, you must make a full-thickness incision beneath the pubic hairs, as described previously; then open the two leaves of one tent-like structure, as I have said. The procedure should be done according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise master prepares all his power to bring back the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of work and tools in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	And suddenly from the pubic region
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion happens to many men in such a manner that the skin above is stuck with the white of the eye, and it cannot move nor perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor beneath the skin and lift it up; and stretch with pincers until you cut what is attached to the delicate spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt so that the patient cannot suffer from the spatula causing injury to the eye; and your incision, from which you scrape away that which is assembled, should be light, so that the skin returns according to its natural shape. And all that assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye they put salty water, and remove it with fresh water and collyrium. Then place a linen tent between the skin and the eye, and place upon the eye wool moistened in dove's dung; and after the third day use collyrium and warm things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It happens that the nail is of two kinds: one is nerve-like and similar to hard fat, and another that is not nerve-like but is like congealed white moisture; when touched with iron it can be grasped with tweezers, but none can be taken. Both sorts begin near the large lachrymal gland and gradually grow until they cover all sight and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: The patient places their head in your hand and opens their eyes; then lift the paper with your hand, grasp the nail with tweezers of small diameter, stretch it upwards. Then take a needle, and insert one horsehair or cow hair or ox hair into it, along with a strong thread; bend the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing it completely with the needle, then tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape away the skin on both sides of the nail that covers the pupil and reaches up to the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the lachrymal gland using the finest spatula and forceps, leaving the natural flesh in place so that the body's usual path for tears is not affected; sometimes the nail is stretched only onto the needle point or thread as we have said; then scrape it away with a soft spatula as described above.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the scalpel does not touch the soft flesh and tear it, and that the probe is not pierced; and after the incision, sprinkle a bit of ground celery seed into the eye, and make collyrium from litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat what needs to be treated until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not brittle and you cannot insert the needle, nor can the tweezers enter, often this type of nail is cured by medicines; they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see it covering, then open the eye of the patient, and take a light cut with the scalpel according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully lift the nail upwards, and if you see that it is not thinning out and the root is pressing against it, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and ground celery seed, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin the same work again according to this same operation, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing stands in your way with the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it with milk, and first cure the hot abscess until it is clean, then resume the work as before until it is clean.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eye harms it greatly, then suspend a sponge there and cut off part of it but not all, so that no tear fluid comes forth; then drip into the eye red collyrium made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Sometimes in the eyes of some people there grows red flesh which covers the pupil and sticks to the paper and turns towards the front, resembling a pterygium; and the treatment for this is that the patient should put their head in your hand, then open their eye, and coil all that flesh with suitable tweezers and hold it firm; then cut off the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting with scissors right up to the end, but take care not to injure the eye during this procedure. And the incision should be made with the spatula that we have mentioned for the trimming of the nail and the removal of small skin growths, as shown in the form after this chapter; and once the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then wash the eye with crushed barley or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines onto it, and press cotton soaked in egg white over the eye to ensure that no hot abscess forms. And if anything remains and hot blood overflows and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with things that soothe hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and do likewise for any other flesh that has grown in the eye like this.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless you must gentle the treatment of each weak eye with natural means; and with accidental means, use iron tools; and do not touch your hand to any of these works until you see that these members can withstand this work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before these veins are red and cover the eye, they impair its work and weaken it every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore it is your duty first to examine whether the eye in which there is white matter is prominent and if there is no other disease present besides whiteness; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then suspend these veins all around according to your wisdom, and let the bandages be doubled subtly in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two bandages placed at each end of the body in this form
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then gently press those veins thus and squeeze out the blood bit by bit until you see the veins move away from the eye; guard that you do not cut the eye with the points of the tweezers, and perform this work at midday before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not damage anything but those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains of the whiteness.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot seize all of it at that hour, then apply a plaster to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pain is eased and the boil is assuredly hot, then begin again according to this manner which is written before until it is healed; and this is the form of treatments.
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls a fistula "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and hot burning medicine according to what I have said before, but it is not healed, there is deceit in it, so you must cut into the boil where it should break open and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is bare.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is bare and you see the corruption and darkness there, then take all the instruments that are here in this form; and it is called "sharp knife," and should be made of hard iron to its head, and pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the site of the rotten bone, then twist it between your two hands and press with your hand a little until you know that this decay has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the site is solid and flesh does not grow, and the body of the bow is solid, and it remains thus for 40 days without renewing or becoming inflamed, and no bad accident occurs there, know that it is healthy; if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring back the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: namely, you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill of this shape, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the drill be tapered to its tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the eye socket, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then twist the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the wind coming in if they hold their hand over their nose. Then restore the site with drying medicines as I have instructed, and when the flesh grows and the site hardens, then the matter will go to the nose; this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens entirely and nothing disturbs it or reduces its size, then you must bandage the patient; then cleanse the eye, then place leeches or cupping glasses without injury to suck, then apply a poultice of acacia and aloe and frankincense and nard on the eye, and then cover the eye with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, double each in four, and then place one on top of another according to how much the eye needs it; then bind it firmly from above with a hard bandage, and begin again with the leeches or cupping glasses without injury to suck; then remove the leeches or cupping glasses and keep the eye bound day and night, and if the poultice becomes moist, then you must remove it quickly; then remove the poultice after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then begin again with the emplastrum and cloths and poultice and leeches or cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	In tearing of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When tears appear in woven cloth, then open it up, and the threads will come apart like grains of resin, which is frightening to see. Therefore, if you wish to repair it, the work is such that you take a needle and insert it into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then take another needle where there are double threads in the frame; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its arrangement; then cut at the place of the double thread and tie one part of the woven fabric around it, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and place a piece of wet linen over it like an egg; and let it remain until the threads stick with the woven fabric, then treat the wound with soothing substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is held in each part by a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great prominence, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from the front of the eye, and remove the moist albume, lower the eye, and insert it quickly; then extract until it is clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the eyebrow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called 'alcunnati' is nothing other than a gathering of bile in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water. And the manner of its appearance in the work is as follows: make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take his head between your two hands, and move him thus until you see the eyebrow rise above your eyes; then insert the probe there, and do not let it descend or obscure the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the eyebrow is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the patient is seated between your hands, then take the spatula and cut along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown until the bow emerges; and when it has emerged, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then dress it with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have shown the likenesses of the waters in the divisions, and what is necessary to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from light for the sun, and bind the healthy eye strongly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if it is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if it is right; then put the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a barleycorn into that blister of the eye at the lesser lachrymal part, then push the instrument called "almagda" gently and turn your hand until it pierces the blister of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be to the depth of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in this paper through the clarity of the cornea, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it under one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If water flows downwards, then the patient sees before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, if the water rises up the second path, place the funnel with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently extract the sponge by rotating your hand bit by bit; then apply a drop of gemstone water to the eye, and lift the eyelid from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye a wool wick moistened in rose oil and egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we put crushed commin on top with egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the sponge cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are men whose eyes are too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberti," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And thus pierce the conjunctiva only slightly, not too deeply but make it subtle, then insert the sponge as we have said; and upon completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable bed where he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and keep him free from all movements, feed him light foods, prevent him from moving his head to the right or left, bind him according to his position until the third day; then untie him in that same dark room, test his sight, and let him see some objects, then rebind him until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of treatment or after incision has begun, but rather alleviation is needed because water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess has formed, you should lance it on the seventh day before and apply ointment that reduces inflammation; once it is soothed, remove the dressing and cover it with a bandage for several days, ensuring it remains in darkness.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then gradually leave the house, return to your usual routine; know that no disciples should interfere with this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And someone came to us from the East who told us that in that region they make a device called an almagda for filtering water, but I have never seen one in our land nor read about it in ancient books; perhaps it is something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda for those who do not know them, and they should be made of proper bronze.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their heads should be of this same fineness, and the rear with three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	Of flesh on bone
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes diverse flesh joints are born on the bones, of which some seem like scorpians with many feet; and there are such where there is flesh enchanted with foul color, and soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, in that flesh which is soft and not enchanted, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, pour oil onto that flesh, and rub it on; then scrape off with a scalpel as much as you can sustainably, until you know that all the flesh is gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be scraped off, then open it with all the delicate instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you being mounted or aposteme closed, do as is necessary; and if they are malignant apostemes, hurry up and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all the flesh is gone, then pour onto the bone a little oil and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is sound; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is bone growth in the upper jaw, preventing tools from cutting properly: therefore, you must insert a thread of somewhat thick linen, dyed dark blue with indigo, with about one or less span between each knot; and let the patient hold the head of the thread in his nostril with some force, and draw it out while smelling until it comes through the nostril into the mouth; children at school often do this, and it is an easy thing for whoever wishes to do it; then hold one end of the thread that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull gently in turns, as we who are experienced do.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have rotted away that flesh, then pull out the thread, squeeze out the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and reinsert it into the nostril as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has rotted away all remaining flesh; and then place a hot cautery made of lead in the nostril for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the tool for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it's made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a candle, with the wick also; and if you wish, make it enclosed like a candle, and let the utensil be full to purge the head; and have many holes at the top to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the bone
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called 'telul' appears on the head of the bone and grows large until it is visible; therefore you must cut it at its beginning and remove all furrows, then apply the cautery or burning medicine. But if it is delayed to be cut until it becomes large, pay attention if it is hard, dark colored, and lacks sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an infected boil that brings great harm to the patient when cut; but if the boil has a soft texture, not dark colored, and can be completely cut out, then the patient will recover without fear of infection. After cutting, treat the wound with drying and constricting remedies.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when swelling occurs in one of these cartilage operations, it does little good unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sew the two lips together at a stitch, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must scrape all the parts of their kernel until they heal, then assemble the two lips at a stitch, and bind them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and crushed incense; and place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is as follows: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For many people, hard abscesses appear inside the lips, resembling grains of millet, small and large; therefore you must turn the lips and cut on each knot, taking it with tweezers and cutting in every part; then sprinkle powdered vitriol in the place after incision until the blood is stanched; and then apply a poultice of mustard, and cure the place with dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
