Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh adheres to the gums, which the ancients call 'albus'; therefore you must hold it with forceps and cut at its root, allowing the blood to flow freely; then put powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders on the place; and if that flesh returns after incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not return after being cauterized; these are the tools used for cutting.
des sordens	of disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes tartar accumulates at the front of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and sharp scales that are ugly; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-brown and worm-like, so much that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth stink; thus you must make the patient sit down between your hands, and their head be in your lap, and scrape the tartar off until nothing remains; and likewise for darkness and green color, and yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if what was done on the first day is correct, that's good; but if not, then start again on the second day and third day, until you have everything scraped; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments to scrape according to what the work shows, because the shape of the scraper used to clean between teeth is different from those used to scrape tartar off the front of teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a toothache that you delay pulling it out as long as you can, because this should not be done at all; for it is a very noble substance until there is no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to have the tooth pulled, you must be certain about the wobbly tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain leaves the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled; yet still the pain does not depart, until the bad one is extracted, for we have seen this happen often. And when you are sure about the wobbly tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides. Then move it slightly with your thumbs or fine forceps bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the forceps; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take some of these tools and gently place them on each side, and use the lever as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and loose, you must fill the hole with bandages where the piercing occurred; and gently grasp it with forceps so that it does not break while extracting; and there must be much bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure not to break it off and leave a piece behind, for then the patient will experience greater pain due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And do not act like the ignorant barbers who through haste and recklessness sometimes break off the root and fail to perform what we have mentioned; but they often cause great illness through neglect of the roots that remain or breaking off the root, as we have seen many times. And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the tools with which one first moves the teeth should be long-pointed and thick-necked, so that they do not double over when you pull on the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend while pulling, and made of good iron and well-made, and serrated for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during pulling, you must place on the spot a small piece of cotton moistened with butter for one or two days,
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the spot is softened, then insert the tongs called 'algefri', with which the head resembles a parrot's beak; and let them be hollowed out inside like a file, this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots still will not come out with all these tongs, then uncover the flesh all around the root, and insert the instrument called 'althali', that is to say, a lever; this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by this, that is good; if not, then help yourself with all the tools, of which the forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And also use this tool that has two rings, of which there is a drawing here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron implements that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and of this tool that resembles large tongs, of which there is a drawing here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this tool be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many tools for teeth; and also other tools that are not listed here; and the wise master finds his own tool according to what his works and the sickness show him, for there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach any tool due to their diversity. And if one breaks the cartilage or the other bones where it could fit, then he seeks out the tools that are needed, which I have told you about, and helps himself with gestures, of which there is a drawing here:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so it does not slip away but can hold and remove it; then restore it to its proper place with appropriate medicines. And if there is rot in the bone, even if it is small, remove it all with this instrument
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	If teeth appear not according to the body's natural shape and their form is ugly, especially in virgin women, it is necessary for you to know if the tooth is too close behind the tooth and not in its proper place, so that neither pulling nor filing can be done: then scrape it; and if it is against the tooth, take this instrument of which there is a shape here, resembling a small beak made of steel sharpened on top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike the cap gently day after day to harden the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent enough to be filed, then file it with a fine file like this one.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the whetstone on which needles are made; and on this stone one should strike the tooth gently and frequently over several days until it ceases to move. Then, at the end, smooth it with any blade or rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, one must grind its sharpness until it is even so that it does not wound the tongue nor distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth lock, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot bite down on food without it hurting, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but it is ineffective, then one must constrict them with a gold thread, for silver threads become green and rot, but gold never changes. The thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth. And if you see that the teeth are crooked, take the thread and double-ended pliers, place them between two healthy teeth, then insert the ends between the loose teeth, one or more, until it reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start wrapping again from where you began, tightening your hand subtly but firmly so that they do not move. And secure the knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers and bring them together, then place them between the sound teeth without injuring the tongue; then hold it as tight as possible until it can remain there, and if it loosens or the threads break, then bind it with another thread; thus it will remain and serve throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the two sound teeth and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, one should replace it in its place gradually, as we have said; and only those who are wise and skilled should undertake this, and sometimes a tooth made of cow bone is fashioned and placed where there is a gap, and it is secured as we have described, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this tie occurs naturally under the tongue at birth or due to a healed wound; and its treatment is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your lap and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve tie from its width until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is any hardness or knot, which is from a healed wound, then insert the nail and cut it from its width; and make sure that the incision is not too deep to avoid damaging the artery beneath; and when you have done so, rinse the area with rose water and hyssop, or cold water, then place a linen cloth under the tongue each night to prevent the wound from healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place powdered vitriol on the wound. If the blood continues to flow, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery that is good for this purpose. Then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a boil that is colored red or black or hard, but the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer. And if it leans towards blenching and there is moisture, throw oncinum powder on it, then make an incision with a sharp scalpel and release it from both sides. If blood flows during your procedure, apply powdered vitriol until it stops bleeding, then return to your procedure until all the boil has been treated. Then lift the wound with silk thread and needle, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes small lumps called 'godath' appear in the throat, which are properly called tonsils. When you treat them as we have described in our division, and they do not heal, beware: if it is a hard abscess with a red color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but let it become ripe, and then you will break it where it would naturally break; and if it is white in color and the root is subtle, have the instrument ready to cut, but first make sure that the abscess is warmly resting and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit facing the sun, with their shoulders in your lap. Open the mouth and take the tongue between your hands, pressing it down with this instrument, whose shape is shown here. It should be made of silver or fine brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument and see the abscess, take the lancet and insert it into the root of the abscess, then twist it upwards as much as possible. Draw out some of the pus with it, then cut the abscess with the instrument whose shape is shown here, resembling a pair of forceps; but their tips are bent towards each other, sharp, made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, then use tongs instead, of which there is a diagram here.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same manner, and afterwards the patient should gargle with warm water and salt water, and if bleeding occurs, the patient should gargle with water in which granet apple skins or myrtle leaves have been cooked, or similar things, until the blood is staunched. Then dress the wound until it is clean. And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them also in this manner similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was almost entirely inside her throat, namely one about the size of a pea. Her throat was nearly completely closed so that she could not exhale through the obstructed passage, nor could she eat or drink, and if she had remained like this for one or two days she would have died.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was then so large it had been placed between two rains through two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hastened and placed one incising iron into the first hole of the nose, then drew it out with great effort, taking along a large portion of skin; then I inserted another iron through the other hole of the nose, opened its mouth, and pressed down on its tongue; after that, I inserted the iron into this abscess, cut off one part, and only a little blood came out; thus, the passage to the woman's throat was opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and for a long time, I did not cease cutting at this abscess; and yet the abscess continued to grow back, filling up the place that I had emptied, becoming very large again; therefore, I cauterized it inside the throat: thus, it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; but if it is below and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the main abscess has calmed down, but it is subtle, then you must cut it out; and that which is round and gathered but not long; and if it is sanguineous or of a reddish color or black, then you must avoid incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient thereby.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to its appearance and length, make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, draw it out underneath, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of both mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more fire than the surplus that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two kidneys, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use something at the cautery for the senses that cause fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is acute heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, cauterizing with a thin iron heated with fire, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and with this movement of the instrument, here is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has at its head a small vessel where you put the medicine, like a spoonful of water, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eyelid. And let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus flow out of their mouth away from the medicine, so that it does not reach the throat or the eye. Then hold your hand over the medicine for the length of half an hour, until you see it turn black and the burning sensation of the medicine has ceased. And if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton onto the eyelid until the cotton touches the eye. Repeat this several times until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, do so, and afterward wipe around the eyelid with cotton soaked in butter, clean what has gathered from the medicine; and rinse with cold water, gargle until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more delicate than incision or cautery. If treated by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and dittany and similar herbs, and gather them all together or some of them into one pot, and place it upon it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument made like this.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or brass, and let one of the heads be placed in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor reaches the ulcer through the canal, until the ulcer is killed. Afterwards begin again often until the ulcer becomes dry, and make sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen there; and do not do it too late after the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and place an egg shell on its head, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the egg shell does not let steam burden the mouth, and it is good treatment together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there is a bone or fish spine stuck in the throat or any other thing. Therefore you must pull out those that you can see, and press the tongue with sunlight using all the instruments so that you may see the movement of the thing; and those that you cannot see and are lodged in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will be expelled by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of flax, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread, tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches its place, it will catch on, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And bend the instrument towards its tip so that it may enter the throat more easily, and hold your head up high; and ensure you do not touch the epiglottis, so as not to cause choking, nor push the bone inside; let the patient themselves insert the tool, so they know where the thing is inserted; if it enters too deep, draw it out evenly along its entire length until it is fully withdrawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the opening of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never treat the wound in the throat with medicine as I mentioned earlier by applying remedies. But if this does not help, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, and press their tongue down using the tool I mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it out with tweezers or fine forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hollow reed and insert it into the patient's throat, then heat the tip of the reed with red-hot iron and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand frequently. As soon as the patient senses the water, they will faint.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if they do not faint as we have said, then fumigate the patient with acacia gum using the same instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times, for they will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The manner of fumigation is as follows: Take a pot with live coals in it, cover the pot with a cloth pierced in the middle, and place the head of the instrument in that hole. Then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient should put the end of the tube into their mouth and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes directly to the lungs. The patient will faint now, and if they do not, repeat the fumigation many times. Let the patient feel thirsty, eat salty foods, and drink no water. Then it will be necessary for them to release by this means.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to remove the vein is this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a crow's beak, and it has sharpness like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, as remembered here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two ways about it, one being in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that arise in joints; and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil has matured according to its completion; and there are others that must be pierced when they are ripe, even if they do not die according to their completion, like those near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses appear near joints, and they are left until they are entirely corrupted, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be damaged, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the main limb, if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb. If it is near the fundament, it should be perforated before it ripens; and it is not necessary to perforate a hard abscess without digestion completed, except for that which is near the fundament, so that it does not penetrate too deeply and become fleshy inside, causing fistule; nor can it heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the sign of the perforation of an abscess that is ripe according to its completion, which is when the pain has ceased, and the fever has departed, and the pain and redness have decreased, and from the bursting and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs. And it is necessary that you make the perforation in a place more dependent than the abscess, where it opens most; and let the perforation be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, and in all places similar without wrinkles.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where it rains, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, so it is worth moving that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick it before this time, then the body will be filled with its venom, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the lips harden and deepen.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring small holes for small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut with the heart, and cover them; when they have become as hard as stone, and softened, then one should do like one does for boils: and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such whose skin is cut like a fig leaf, like abscesses of the armpits; and there are such where a round incision is made, and other incisions with similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as soft superficial abscesses, you must pierce them clearly; and when the abscess is large, and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once, but draw out part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out more again later; do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out. Similarly if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or elderly decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	However, if the arrow suddenly jumps out with the exit of the pus, which by chance causes the patient's death, and you are not aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore proceed with great caution in this chapter. After you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is small, then dress it with bandages of linen or old cotton. If it is a large abscess with many openings, then you must stuff each one with a bandage so that they come together. And if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and scraped it around, then you must fill it with dry cotton or lint without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is discharge of blood from your work, then bring cold water and quickly, wet a cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the discharge of blood persists, then bring aid and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book in many places. And if it is wintertime, and the place where the abscess is very sensitive, then you should put warm cloths soaked in wine and oil on it. And if it is summer, and the place is fleshy, then you should put cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and cleanse and dress it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is how one must universally know about the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is that chapter.
des soros	Of sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When boils come on the head, they are small abscesses, and their appearances are similar to those in cloths, like the yolks of an egg, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some of them are fatty and have moisture like chicken, and some are hard and stony at the cutting, and there is no doubt that if an artery opposes them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you examine with all instruments called "entromissoirs," from which the form comes hereafter, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, cut along its length above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scrape without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns again if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and dress the wound, leaving it until the next day.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recommence the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you know well that it does not remain in the night; then treat the wound with suitable ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds much matter, then incise it according to this form: make a long cut; cast your lint thereupon, and excoriate it on all sides, and take great care to draw out the coat which lies underneath it. And if the artery opposes you, do as I told you after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise treat an abscess if it is hard, by incising and draining it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting into a hard and moist abscess makes it easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses that have no moisture at their head, and if among those I incised was an abscess found at the head of an old woman: it was as hard, sharp, and white as a pebble, and could not be broken; had one struck it with any force, it would have made as great a wound as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other swellings occurring on the head, especially those that come from the heads of children and the roots of ears, the incision should be made as close to the dependent position as possible, so that the bow may easily exit; and treat it as is proper.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these swellings occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin area, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and there are many of them, intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located within its own flesh, like the nut and the swelling on the head, as we have said; and there are many similar kinds of these swellings.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some contain moisture, and some are malignant that do not yield to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	If you see one that has a good appearance to the touch, and is similar in color to the flesh, and moves freely on all sides and is not hard against the nerves of the neck or the artery or the vein, and is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and scrape off each part, and hold back the two lips of the wound with forceps if necessary, as we have said for head swellings; and treat it little by little, and make sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use a dull or cutting knife, so that your hand does not slip, and do not cut too deeply, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow you to operate, put powdered vitriol into the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and compress the wound; leave it thus until the abscess quiets down, and the wound softens, and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And once the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until it is completed. Then examine your finger for any small boils that may remain, cut them and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the boil, do not cut that boil at its base but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off on its own without harm. Then dress the wound with Egyptian ointment-soaked cotton wool, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut off the entire boil, then bring together both lips of the wound and stitch them up immediately, ensuring there is no excess flesh remaining due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary for you to understand how to cover the root of him, and draw fire, and sew up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold excessiveness, pierce where it opens more; and pierce in the same manner as the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then bring ointments with tents and similar things so that they corrupt those that remain of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment gently to the flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	Of sciatica
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and that is their writing.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have sciatica, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and help should not be given by them because all the veins and the membrane of the patient are hot in the mouth or throat or both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the stomach, it is necessary to lift the epiglottis to avoid suffocation that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should do so below three circles or four, through a small slit crosswise between two circles or by the quantity of the soft palate slit, not in the cartilage; and these locations are suitable for sectioning the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long on each side.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat entirely, then cut towards the heart until it reaches the channel; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then lift the soft palate, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the opening of the windpipe of the channel that spurts forth from the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a short time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, join together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew up the whole without cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, when the fault will appear.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore cut off the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow and breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death. And therefore the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the worst of the disease passes, which it does in three or four days. And then they commanded the wound to be sewn up and dressed until it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the artery, and I was called to treat her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that it had not cut vein nor drawn fire except in the throat, and the wind escaped through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed the wound closed, healing it until it was clean; and nothing happened to the damsel except that she lost her voice briefly, which then returned to its former state. Therefore, I say there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it appears as a large, dark-colored swelling, most common in women. It can occur in two ways: naturally or accidentally. The natural type has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type occurs in two ways: one resembles a boil under the skin, and the other is similar to an abscess caused by an artery. There is fear when it is large, but it need not be opened with fire except for the smaller ones; first probe and search with the intrument all around it: if you find it like a fatty boil that does not adhere to any vein, cut it like a boil, and remove its covering completely if there is one. Then carefully examine everything and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many types of us there are, which I shall describe all their appearances; now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is warm and holds fever until the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then fever and warmth subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is neither warmth nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the flesh, and begins like a bag, and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and many colors they have as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of us, it is necessary that you first examine and inquire with all the instruments that are called “entromissoire,” according to what its form will be in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into the apostemes of us is that you take in the moistest place that you find in the aposteme, and twist your thumbs little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the aposteme; then extract the entromissoire, and beware lest it leap forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture has a color, then lance it just like you would other abscesses; and if after the insertion there is no moisture, know that it is mature, so cut it in cross fashion, grasp it with forceps, lightly scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you can pull it out whole along with the root; and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out piece by piece until none remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	But if something remains, the boil will return many times; and if a small piece remains and blood causes you grief, then dress the wound with some caustic waters, bind the wound tightly, apply soothing poultices for hot abscesses, and continue treating it until it is healthy; and if the boil is large, cut the two lips of the wound open, and treat those that have entered flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or another, then quickly apply powdered vitriol to its place and leave it for two or three days until the wound has rotted away and bleeding subsides; then return with tweezers to remove what remains of the root.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments inserted; there are three kinds: large, medium, and small. There are three squares called "albaret", one called "breb". They are also like needles used to sew sutures, made of tin, iron, or silver. Those that are yellow are more valued, but black lead is more preferred for encircling fistulas. There are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of forceps are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small. There are also forceps with two loops of three kinds each, and those with three loops, which are also of three kinds. There are also forceps with one loop only, which are of three kinds; all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are cutting, and there are some that do not cut much more than one side. With them, one scrapes the nerves so that one does not injure the vein or the nerve. And among these intromissive instruments are the alembics placed in hands, such that the patient is unaware at the opening of abscesses. And they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in charred flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places; and sometimes another instrument is made, like a fist-sized scraper, according to this shape, with which blood is stanched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes it is placed at the location where there has been injury of veins and arteries, and some are made according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must do it according to this form from line .b. to line .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat, and dress the wound with medicine between flesh, then bring together both lips of the wound to suture, and care for it until it is healed. And if the breast leans downwards, softened by its greatness as happens in women, open it into two ribs above through two similar incisions; such that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape away the skin between both lips, and remove the fat, and dress with what we have mentioned about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in healing, until it is healed. And if it is not healed, or if the incision was not fully made because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; leave it until it has digested the remaining and fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of armpit boils
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These armpit boils are types of hard scrofula with rough edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be incised according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once the entire boil is emptied, fill the wound with soft cotton and leave it overnight. Then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment until healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the boil is similar to scrofula, incise it as we have said for scrofulous ulcers. If the wound becomes inflamed, apply a cautery as we have mentioned previously.
de la routure de l’artere	Of arterial rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is closed off, many boils often form. The same happens when a vein bursts with a boil. If one recognizes this, the boil will be long and deep; if you press on it with your fingers, you will feel throbbing. If it's due to a vein, the swelling will appear red and shiny. It is foolish to incise this boil, especially when it is located under the armpits, angles of joints, around the neck, or in many other places where it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid cauterization with iron, and the one who is at the head should also avoid it. In the case of an arterial swelling under the skin, cut above it; then incise along the length, carefully separating the artery from its surroundings until it is exposed. Then insert a needle underneath it and push it through to the other side. Tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you for the extraction of two temples arteries. Then use an intromitter to prick the point between the two ties so that the blood flows out and the abscess is drained. Then treat the wound with appropriate ointments until it heals; if the abscess is due to vein incision, you must carefully cut away everything that can be cut from the abscess throughout the skin, then insert the needle under the point held by your hand, push it through, and tie it with a double thread so that it can be pulled out on the other side. Then bind the abscess as I have told you, using one of the two knots tied with the thread. If you doubt whether the threads will slip, insert another needle under all the threads along the entire abscess where the first needle was cut, and tie them in four places. Then cut away the excess from the abscess and also cut away the excess flesh, leaving only what is bound. Finally, place a cloth moistened with wine and oil on it, then treat it with compresses and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of blackheads
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Likewise blackheads come to the arteries and veins when they are struck, or from too much exertion, and similar causes.
