Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin area, as we have mentioned, and the location opens up. And no part of the intestines comes out at first, but if some do come out, it is little and can be repaired quickly. But if it remains too long in this state, the wound or abscess grows until the intestines come out. This happens due to the expansion of the vein that is in the groin area, as we have mentioned, because it becomes stretched, then softened and swollen with the location opening up. And the cure for this is cauterization, as we have said before. And sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the opened vein of the rupture at its widest point according to its size, then extract the vein that is under the skin next to it. Then take a reed and place it on the opening of the vein, then press it into the depth of the abdomen. Then sew up the two openings of the vein on top of the reed's head, sewing both together. Then remove the reed's head, and do not cut or stretch the vein nor anything else, as I have explained to you in the treatment of intestinal rupture. Then treat it with wound care.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, so cleanse it and heal the wound until it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sinew is tight and has no appearance in the fracture; cauterization is muted here, closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	due to softening of the skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints in some men becomes softened because the flesh inside is softened, and it is easy to see. And it is necessary, when one wishes to treat it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then bring together the two edges with a suture, and if you wish, first sew up the excess softened skin with three or four stitches firmly. Then cut between the sutures and dress it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the threads.
dou chastrement	on castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castrations are prohibited by our law, and therefore I would like not to speak of it in this book. However, it is necessary to know two things: firstly, the doctor should know how to respond when asked about it and how to perform the operation; secondly, because we often have need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, dogs and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that dressings are made in two ways: either by attraction or by splitting open.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method that we perform by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water until the joints are softened and limp. Then you grasp them with your hand so they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the dressing of the flank: you must first shear the beast and press the skin of the joints with your left hand. Then tie the suspensiony ligament and cut each joint cap one time after carefully scraping it clean, leaving a little fat on the sinews and subtendinous tissues that are over the vessels. This method of dressing is milder than that done by attraction because some things from the joints may remain during attraction, causing the beast to desire lust. Then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	On hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways among men: one way is when between the two testicles opens an aperture like the figure of a woman's genitals, sometimes with hair around it and occasionally urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is thus in women, which they have on the vulva like a wand and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is thus: you should clean all joined wounds and dress them as other wounds. For the second manner, in men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no remedy.
de la tentigene	Of inflammation
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Inflammation is a joined wound on the natural part which is too ugly to behold; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you cut off the superfluity of inflammation with your hand or pincers, and clean it gently; but do not go too deep lest bleeding occur, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. And there is another wound which appears at the mouth of the uterus and the anus, sometimes it emits pus, and resembles a cow's udder, hence the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cut it, as we have indicated for tenacious wounds, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Wandering is when the nature of woman is not pierced, or the passage is narrow; and it is innate by birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred there; or it is caused by flesh adhering, or by thin, dense, or thick skin, and it extends deeply into the uterus, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception and childbirth, and sometimes menstrual flow; and its recognition comes from examining the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swellings are close to the surface, press them with your two fingers or your hand.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is due to thin skin and is close to the labia majora, act quickly and proceed thus: place your two index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the labia minora firmly until the thin skin is taut and covers the swelling; then take wool soaked in oil and apply it to the area, and have the woman lie down gently each day so that it does not stick.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the shoulder blade is hard and thick, then you must cut it like a bay leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is flesh-born, then suspend it with oil and cut it; and have at hand medicines that staunch blood, such as aloe, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with an egg; then apply a broad bandage of lint so that the wound does not close; and thus let it remain for some time, and cover it with a dry linen cloth; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh comes out in the marrow, then it must be cut according to this manner, unless it is an inflamed boil.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed boil that is in the marrow, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are abnormal openings of veins which without custom do not exist, and when hemorrhoids become old they become hard; we have already mentioned in the division their similarities, signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that piles and hemorrhoids, when deeply embedded in the flesh and not apparent upon feeling, are not suited for treatment with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those located at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold house, then heat the cautery with tongs, and apply it to its roots. Then sprinkle powder made from medicines that constrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense and similar things. Then leave her feet at the fire for an hour, then place her in cold water. If bleeding occurs, seat her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar things. Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and celery, and make a poultice to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she hemorrhages, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply bloodletting cups to the back and breasts without cutting; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or celery juice with old wine, and apply at the location.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the boil has softened, then dress the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a bitter head, so it should be covered as I said earlier; and then dress it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	Of boils on the buttocks
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of boils occur on the buttocks, such as cancer and piercing boils, herpetic sores, inflamed boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot boils, along with many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must describe in this treatise the hot boil that appears on the buttocks, which is not one of those boils that suppurate; and if you wish to know how to work with iron, observe whether the boil is aggravated at the beginning of its appearance, and filled with heat and fever, and becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not rush to pierce, but make it bleed until the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where they can lean back, and support their back and bring their feet together behind the leg; and let their thighs be spread apart, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them securely with a good bandage; then suck the boil towards the right side, and bring in the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the mare, about which there will be more later; and it is necessary that when you bring in this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the mare, so that what enters inside does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then one must cover the depth of the mare with rags, so that the instrument does not hurt; and it is necessary that they put the horn of the instrument above, and wet the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the abscess opens and you cut it gently with your hand, then you must cover its head with spongy lint; and when the bowels are emptied, you should place moistened lint in oil of roses or dried oil into the wound; and put lint moistened with hot water on the marrow of the bone, and place clean linen cloths moistened in water or boiled mallows around it; then treat after two days with suitable ointment until healed; and sometimes lift the marrows and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then with water where lily roots and long aristologes have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has reached the marrow, you must beware of cauterizing with a hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and you know when to see the woman pressing downwards, and desiring to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out forthwith. Then know that this birth is according to nature's figure, and the head is presented first, with the afterbirth accompanying it; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child may be born quickly; for when it descends upon its head, then comes the afterbirth with it, and the marrow is cleaned of its impurities by good cleansing. But if it comes otherwise, it does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because sometimes it happens on his feet, and heat comes to the body or shoulders, and hands, or it happens on his belly, or sometimes, and by chance they are turned onto his neck, and in other unpleasant shapes; therefore it is necessary that the doctor be wise and skillful in these matters, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto his head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth crying, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or have women hold her; and raise her nature with oil or fenugreek cooked, and then place the little spatula between her shoulders, of which this is the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and scrape with her nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must enema the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and oil; then make her sneeze with condisium, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are stuck out, you must gently push them back bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high; then tilt the seat onto the ground, ensuring she does not fall during this process; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the ankle that is positioned beforehand, and extract the child, realigning it properly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the exit of the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, you must push it up high; then turn it gently bit by bit until it is aligned properly; then take one of its feet and stretch it out gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, then command her to grasp it, and cause it to sneeze with condition; if it jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then turn it gently bit by bit until it is in accordance with its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Because then it is easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if the fire does not come as we have described, then take musk from a male deer, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in one mortar; and put this ointment on the nature of the woman's womb, then let her sit in warm water up to below her breasts; and when she is warmed below, let her wear a girdle of myrrh and place it below her, letting it remain for an hour; then let her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose shut, and gently take the baby out because now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the exit of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, then the midwife should gently place her hands on it; then support its head and let the feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; and fold its hands gently and then put them on the belly, and remove the pillows below to allow it to come out properly; and if the child does not come out, take its feet and move it forcefully, then move the belly up, then place your hands underneath; and gently pull the child; and tell the woman to push as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the childbirth issue where a hand comes forth.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to attempt to reposition the hand: if it cannot be repositioned, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie down on the bed, and hold her legs wide apart; then apply the ointment that I have described; and if she does not give birth, seat her on a chair, then attempt to reposition the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural form, make her sneeze, and instruct her to bear down until the infant is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Regarding the issue of a child born face up with its hands spread out and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to take her hand and gradually turn the child, bringing it out easily; and when it is aligned, apply the ointment of olive oil and musk that we have described, then instruct her to move gradually; and once this has been done, seat her on a chair and instruct her to bear down, making her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, it applies to all joints.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When fire comes in this way to all joints, cut the joint with your finger until the moisture is emptied; and if the child leans on its face and neck, then cut from below so that it is not retained, and the child will die. Then put the child back in place until you have positioned it correctly, and instruct the woman to take any position: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born frequently, and sometimes three or four are born at once; this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that two are born and do not live if they are named. I know those that are multiplied are separated by the caesarean section made by the surgeon who cuts them loose from below. And sometimes they also come out naturally like any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out loudly, then heal them as we have said, and let the surgeon be skilled, and do quickly and easily what she does; and thus do as it ought to move towards health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No more than one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or several up to fifteen are formed in the womb, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the sage's compass. And it is necessary that the surgeon know all this, for perhaps similar things have happened; so do accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and no force comes forth, and you are compelled by necessity to use your hands. Then you must know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or fears death. Then let the woman lie on her back, with her head hanging down and legs raised. And the assistant hold her thighs, or tie her to the bed so she is not moved during the removal of the child. Then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oil mixed with altee and fenugreek seeds and linseed, then the surgeon covers his hands with these oils and muscillaiges. Then gently inserts them into the womb, then take one of the tools that are suitable for this, and make sure the child is positioned correctly to descend headfirst. Then insert the tool into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or near the vulva or near the sides, and if it descends feet-first, insert it between the thighs. And it is necessary that he hold the tool with his right hand, and put the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and gently insert it into any of these places we have mentioned until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the tool:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert it against the other side once, or twice if necessary, so that the extraction is even; then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other for easy removal, and make sure the forceps has teeth to hold firmly, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, let the surgeon rub some of his thumbs with oil and place them on that part, then pull from the other side; and if nothing remains, then place this forceps higher up and continue doing so until it is completely free.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to tension, then wrap the cloth around it until it is all out; then place the coping in the joint of the sole or at the wrist, and do likewise for the other hand.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the infant's head is large and the passage is narrow where there is an acute point gathered at the top, then place the spatula between your thumbs and cut the top to remove the point; or use the instrument called 'almidach', whose shape is shown with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one. Do likewise if the child has a large natural head; then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head bulges out but remains tight at the fontanelle, cut it until the moisture comes out from the fontanel; and if it cannot come out, remove it piece by piece as you are able; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or below the ribs, then pierce it until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then traction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the uterus is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or breast, then you must draw it out with a cloth wrapped on your hand; and open the belly or breast until the moisture that is there flows away; and if the other members are removed but the head remains, then place your hand deep into the uterus, and draw it up to the mouth of the uterus; then place one or two fingers in there, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the uterus is narrowed by a hot sore that has come there, then do not work on it, rather apply moist and fatty things; and the physician should use poultices, and softening and soothing waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side and you can make it even, then apply what we have said for the live child; but if you cannot do this, then draw it out piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it should happen that we said in hot abscesses which come to the marrow; and if there is profuse bleeding, then let it be put into boiling water restricting, and let other treatments be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been killed, then another was consulted upon that one, and the other was also killed.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After many years, an abscess appeared on his beard, which swelled so much that it opened, and began to have great discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for treatment, and I thought long and hard, but could not stop the bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a poultice with strong attraction on it, and one bone came out, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly at this, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cleaned the wound and removed many bones until the woman was in much better condition; and the woman lived for a long time thereafter, with a little bit of bowels coming out from that place; and I am telling this story only because when a master finds something strange like this, he should know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the compresser, by which books are opened; and at two turns to both heads of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two inches wide, and the margin one inch thick, and one and a half palms long. And between the two ligaments there should be two joints of this same wood which are fastened on both sides, being half a palm or a little more in length; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the dislocation to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, which is more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, resembling forceps; and it has two joints at both heads, as you can see, each half a palm long and two inches wide. And when you want to open the dislocation with all the instrument, then have the woman sit on the bed, with her feet hanging down and her legs apart, then insert the two joints together into the dislocation, and hold the head of the instrument under her thighs. Then open your hand on the entire instrument, just as you would do with equal forceps, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the dislocation, until the ball comes out as she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the physician has prepared them, the work becomes faster, and more abundant for men by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument until you have prepared it, because its needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is retained during birth, you must command the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with condici powder, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she sneezes well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not succeed, then take a pot, and make an opening in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the pregnant woman, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cumin, and centory; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over the fire. Then put one end of a tube into the pot's opening and the other end into the pregnant woman's mouth, and hold it until the steam enters her. Then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sciatic nerve jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not cured, then order the maidservant to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or musk-rosin, and then place it on the thigh and search for the sciatic nerve. And when she has found it, gently grasp and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the hip does not fall during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pulled; thus it will come forth and relieve itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the hip is very narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs. And if it is not helped by all that we have said, then take care that you do not pull too hard; but it is necessary that what is at the opening of the hip should be tied to the woman's thigh, then perform a clyster with tetrafarmakon oil; thus she will be able to bear it and recover, and come back cured. But still, when she bears it, bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore fumigations are suitable for this, some of the ancients have tried fumigation with mustard and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman at childbirth for the retention of the membranes is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a cage made of glass or similar material. Insert the fine end into the natural opening and place the wide ends over the fire. Use hot coals for the fumigation, replacing the bellows when they become exhausted.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born whose anus has not been pierced and is obstructed by a fine membrane. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her thumb, being careful not to touch the membrane with her fingernails or cut it with a sharp instrument. Then, she should cleanse the area with moistened linen soaked in wine and oil, applying ointment until it is completely healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not remain steadfast, then place in the hole a pin of lead and leave it there for several days, removing it when the child wishes to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this blockage comes from the sudden appearance of a wound or an abscess; therefore cover that suddenly appeared wound: it should be treated as we have said for the pin of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula at the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come beneath the fundament are nodular, and those that grow near the fundament defected, or in the space of the two buttocks, so there is one fistula or several; and when this nodule is ancient, it opens, and produces moist white pus or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by the fact that there is evacuation through them during defecation or flatulence when the patient makes an effort, and sometimes worms come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint, and up to the tip of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the fistula piercing at the fundament, and not merely piercing: and it is that you insert your two index fingers into the fundament, and insert a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula where there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a fine reed or horsehair probe until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, nor does any pus, wind, or vermin come out of the hole as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, so urine flows out, and it cannot be stopped by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces through to the hip joint, then the inflammation extends to that area; if there is no tortuosity and the pain encircles around, then it will be gone soon, and no medicine or salve is needed for this; and in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except effort, and the vain boasting of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	For those which are not Persian and not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it should be done thus: the patient lies on their stomach in your hands; lift their legs up to their thighs, with their thighs inclined towards their belly; then insert a bronze probe, or one of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the inflammation originates.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around their anus, then you should insert your two index fingers into it; if you sense that the inflammation has pierced through there, and if between your fingers you feel either the sphincter or flesh, then know that it is a Persian fistula; do not treat it unless you can heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Some say one can hardly heal any wounds, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one does there, it is heating the cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before; and put it hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; and do this twice or three times, until you know that those broken tissues are burnt, which resemble an feathers quill; and then the cure with soft linen soaked in butter, until that tissue comes off, then the cure with ointment between flesh and wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If healed thus, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise, and if the thread enters but does not reach to the fundament which is between your two fingers, and there is a thick covering of flesh or skin between the thread and you; and you see the fistula through that which covers the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and insert the thread immediately afterwards, and afterward apply the cautery until it reaches the head of the thread; and the thread will be freed and fall away; then remove those burnt tissues which resemble a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood defeats you, and flows between you and your work, cauterize it with fire or hot medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	And the cautery of fire combines two things: that is to say, the burning of adjacent flesh and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture. Then treat wet wounds with burdock or crushed plantain until the affected area becomes dry, and remove burned flesh from the wound; then treat the wound with soothing ointments and powders.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	And when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula extends deep from the foundation, and is distant from the body, push your two fingers into its foundation, and press down.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tension, and between two there is the skin or membrane or flesh where it is about to burst, then make an opening through which there can be trust and hope by using one of these three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut down to its foundation, or if you cannot do that, then place tents and treat it as before; but do not go too deep lest you cut the tissue holding the foundation, and let the discharge flow without intention. Then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Otherwise, remove that covering and cleanse it once it has been cut near the foundation with a tent or other pointed instrument. Then clean the damaged flesh in the wound as much as you can. Then strive to heal the wound, and keep the fistula away from the foundation: this will make things easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: when you insert the probe into the fistula and it is located on the side near the fundament close to the skin above, then take a probe pierced at the tip in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And then twist thread II into I and insert the probe with all of thread II into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces into the margin of the fundament inside, then withdraw the thread from that hole as you would put your finger into the fundament; and pull the head of the thread out, and bring together both ends and tie them together, leaving them for one or two days; and tighten them sometimes until the threads cut through those tissues that are between them and fall off; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in every way that you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to first cauterize deeply and then treat until healed, as we have said.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the narrow spine through which the fistula is made is sharp and cutting on one side, but not on the other because you should not cut what you should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus like grains of resin, being small or large, and constantly discharging blood, with one or several present, or they prolapse from the anus and extend to the tip of the anus; but those that prolapse have less moisture, and often discharge a little yellow water or a little blood, having the color of flesh. The treatment for those who have hemorrhoids inside the anus is as follows: instruct the patient to strain while going to the latrine until the hemorrhoids are forced out, and then seize them with forceps; hurry and grasp them with tongs or hold them with your fingernail, then cut them at their base. If the nail cannot hold them due to moisture, take them with a cloth, cotton, or a piece of chamlet; pull them out with two fingers, then cut them, and apply warm powder like a cautery. Or you can cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cauteries, then treat them with other remedies until healed. If the anus cannot be emptied, administer to the patient a biting and sharp enema to wash what is inside the anus so that it can come out freely. When the patient strains and if the hemorrhoids are already prolapsed from the anus, the treatment is easier: grasp them with your fingernail or tongs, cut them, then treat them as mentioned above until healed, ensuring that there is no incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must prepare the stitching in this manner: take one thread of wool, and put it into a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be loose; and pull the thread firmly, then tie the knot, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one to drain excess blood. Then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate on the wound, and apply it, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them rest until they fall asleep, and when they have fallen asleep, then treat them with ointment and other remedies until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the cleaning of the fire or the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying out of phlegm in the intestines, and due to a constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape the surface with a sharp instrument or your nail, so that it does not become moist; then shave it until it is smooth as it should be; and if it cannot be made smooth, begin scraping again more forcefully than before, until it is bare and completely scraped; then cleanse it until it is healed.
dou fremit	If there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	An ant is a small creature that lives within the body and goes very deep inside it. Sometimes one feels its chill, feeling like death due to trembling, which spreads throughout the body, especially affecting the hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment for this is that you take a quill from an oyster feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that feather on the trembling spot so that its circle covers all around the trembling; then turn your hand along the entire feather until it completely encircles the trembling, pressing it deep inside and pulling out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a strand of brass or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and pointed above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, cauterize the trembling vein, as it is mentioned before in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the shape of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	An enema is sometimes made of silver or lead, or melted brass or iron; and sometimes these tools are made small or large according to the need.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that one uses in caring for children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema is as follows: where the belly is bound, it is like this:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the feces inside pierced; and there should be two holes on one side and one on the other, and the belly should be placed on a beast's bladder or parchment with many small holes around it, with one inch of space between each hole. Then take a strong thread of coarse, twisted yarn and tie it in an X-shape or wrap it around, and close the belly like a goat's stomach. And when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the tool before with a strong thread, then administer the enema; this is the circular shape:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and oil or egg yolk or similar should be rubbed on the end of the clyster before it is inserted gently; then the minister squeezes with both hands until it is completely empty, then removes the clyster, and the patient lifts their legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, then hold it as long as possible; and if it remains overnight undisturbed, there is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use a clyster in an illness with abdominal swelling, and the medicine rushes to come out, then begin again until it is emptied.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, then let the clyster be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the thin clyster tip where the skin is tightened:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and for illnesses, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made from, and according to where the wounds are made, and what they are made of.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, and cutting with sword or knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the locations on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar members. And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then be careful if it was caused by a blow from a stone or similar things, and if the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you are uncertain about raising a hot abscess: make the bandage immediately with the cephalic membrane even if there is little bleeding from the wound, and let the bandage be on the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the patient avoid excess consumption of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not want to heal, let his food be reduced,
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and its lips cannot be approximated by tenting, then approximate them by suture, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and hangs open but still has some attachment, then cut it off. Then treat the wound with medicines, replace the skin with hard tissue, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods such as beans and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the skin but not reaching the bone, cut off all the rotted part and cauterize it with fire. Then treat the wound. And if there is an artery or vein exposed in the wound that cannot be staunched by medicines alone, ligate the artery. If you find it dislocated, tie it down with a thread. And if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy; and it is that you place into this powder that bonds before the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is thus: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them subtly into a powder, and apply it to the wound, binding it tightly until it absorbs well and joins with all its blood; then let it rest without loosening it, unless it swells; for do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes live chalk alone is used when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but before the wound has moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if the wound has moved, especially in summer, then do not apply this powder; instead, place some digested ointments or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey until it swells; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you about head fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head; but if the nerve of the neck or an artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other treatment than to leave it alone and not put anything constraining on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber washed likewise in sweet water, and other moist compresses according to this manner, and moist applications.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it closed and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
