Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full of bowels, then pierce it lower down; and if an artery is cut and blood is flowing copiously, then drain it and close it and cauterize it if necessary. And if the spine of the throat or the heart is cut, guard the passage through which the meat goes, then sew up the heart on top of the windpipe, but do not touch the throat itself; and then bind it tightly and leave it for a few days before treating it with drying ointments until it heals. And if the wound has impressed upon the bone, cut around it; and if there are pieces of bone that you can remove, remove them all, but those which you cannot have, let the wound fester until it can be drained and sewn up. And if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look if wind from the wound blows out when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first, nor bind it so that the blood does not flow deeply and reach the heart, killing the patient; but apply attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so that there will be no spasm, nor harmful trembling of the heart, nor straining of the breath. And when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with dressings and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal or open, know immediately that there is a fistula present; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a cut made by a sword or knife and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat the one that is ahead; if it is large, suture it; if it is small, use powder. If it is close to the bone and has cut into pieces, clean the wound, and remove any foreign bodies if they are evident; if they are not evident, let the wound fester so that extraction will be easier. The judgment for other wounds on other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Regarding rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Rupture of the belly can be large, medium, or small. In the case of a large wound, sometimes the intestines or part of them protrude through it, making stitching difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because it is harder to replace the intestines. For this reason, it is better to close a moderate-sized wound, as moving the intestines back into place can be easier with such a wound. Know that there are four ways in which the belly can rupture: two common stitches occur in abdominal stitching, and two other stitches specific to other wounds on the body are also common; however, they are more specific to abdominal stitching, and I will discuss each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestines is sticking out, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: soak a sponge or one cloth in just hot water, or cook in hot water with cumin and saffron and spikenard, and raise the intestines until the swelling has passed; and sometimes do this wine compress, and it is helpful to apply it with sole for swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling beginning to go down, moisten the intestines with water in which aloe and mallow have been cooked, for by this the entrance will be widened a little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision on the wound using the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is that you cut only if necessary, none should cut without great necessity; and this is the tool for splitting: so cut inward in the curve and do not force too much. Here is the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is widened, and the intestines jut out, then reset them according to their natural shape in their proper place if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	If the wound is wide and it is below the belly, then make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is below the belly, then place the head and breast higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then arrange it so that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus one must prepare this for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	If the wounds are small, apply what you have prepared, then have between your hands one skillful minister who carefully draws out all the ruptured parts with their hand and joins the lips together; this is the common method of stitching. Take several needles according to the quantity of the wound's width, then leave two spans from the head of the wound and insert a needle with good strong thread. Pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the sinew beneath it until you pierce it on that side and join together four heads of sinew; then tighten them with a double thread around the needle on both sides, then carefully join both edges of the wound, leaving two spans, and insert another needle. Then tie the thread as you did the first needle, continuing this process according to your need for needles until the entire wound is restrained. The needles should be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because very fine ones cut all the flesh, and very large ones cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized. Do not pierce the needles too deeply into the flesh and skin so that they do not cut and open the wound before stitching. Then cut off the heads of the needles so they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place tents or bandages on the needle heads to hold them in place, leaving them there until the wound is healed. This method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it only requires one or two needles. The second stitching method is common: join together both sides of the skin and both sides of the sinew with one needle having a medium-strength thread; once you have pierced all four heads together, tighten the needle on that side in the manner one sews cloth, placing the thickness of a finger's span between each stitch. This stitching is known to men; I once stitched a wound on a man's belly that was over a palm wide, and it had protruded intestines about two palms long, with the wound being right in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset his intestines after it had been out for 24 hours. The wound was closed by the 15th day and I treated it; he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians judged that he would die, but this was a miracle. I did not treat it with ointment, as there were none available nor any medicines in this place. Instead, I put old cotton on the wound twice a day and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing: Take the needle and pierce it from the outside towards the inside until it reaches the heart. Then leave the eye of the needle on the outside where you pierced it, and pierce it again from the inside out. The purpose of this stitch is to sew as a furrier sews furs, leaving the needle once on one side and then picking it up again on the other side until the sewing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: some people assemble the two parts naturally and apply one end of the thread to the other in this way: insert a needle into the nearby edge of one piece of skin, then pierce it only at that spot, leaving both ends of the thread; next, turn the needle and pierce it from outside going towards inside across both ends of the thread; then pierce each side from outside going towards inside through two other edges of skin that are located on the opposite side; this is the best and most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some attest to it: one must suture the belly with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be placed on one side, and the other on another, in the manner of those who sew hides. Know that when the wound is inside the belly, the stitching is tighter than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds. It is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood before it has moved, then reset the intestines and close the skin; then place powder made from herb on it, and if it has moved, apply some ointment present until the wound bows; and stitch the fil, and let the sinew and flesh be sound; then treat the wound like others until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then apply old cotton immediately when it begins to bow, and stir it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But in many conditions when wounds are simple, you have no need for other medicine. And if you doubt that the wound communicates with the main limbs, then it is necessary to moisten light linen in warm oil of roses or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which happens often, then give black wine enema; especially if putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines called "jejunum" cannot heal when injured due to the thinness of its veins and the delicacy of the entire body, and their proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back also like the intestines while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned green or black, tie the spot that is black to prevent blood flow since there are veins and arteries here; then cut what is between the ties, and hang the two ends down from below the wound until it falls out to ease extraction, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, as I saw one man wounded in the belly by a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became funnel-shaped, and developed into a fistula through which digested food and wind escaped. I treated it according to what I knew, continually refining my approach until he healed, with the ends sewn together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him bound, I doubted that the patient had illness in his belly. But there was no harm, rather he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; some experimenters said that if there were a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound thus: Take frogs with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the frog has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches open its mouth over them; then cut off its head, and this remains so that it cannot come undone, then place another frog afterward in the same manner before, until the wound is entirely covered; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These frogs are inserted into the intestine and no harm comes to the patient. And one can suture the intestine with a thin thread made from an animal's gut thus: Take the head of this gut thread that is well skinned, and then tie at its head a thin twisted linen thread, then put the thread through the needle, and stitch up the gut, bringing it back together; and this manner of frog sewing is not far outside the path of trust and hope. But if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device or health but that of subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Concerning a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It should be known that any wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is commonly called a 'fistula,' and especially so if it is deep and returns inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is truly a broken and white nodule without pain, and it is also deep like the feather of a bird; sometimes it appears clear and deep, other times thick; sometimes small, other times large. I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no scar only becomes such due to one of nine causes: namely, either because of the thinness or quality of the blood or flesh; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips which prevents flesh from forming; or because there is too much depth; or because the place is narrow and the matter is of poor quality; or because the medicine used in treatment was not good; or because the corruption is in the form of a pestilence; or because the property of the region is tardy in digestion, slow to heal, and naturally inflamed. I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their treatments with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must inform you about the treatment of fistula, which is done by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, nerves, or the sacrum, intestines, bladder, ribs, spine, or any joint of the hands or feet; and some even originate at the primary property of the member itself.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this type are difficult to treat, and require effort and skill. If there is any fistula that does not originate from the locations I mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment and recognize it, then use an iron or brass probe if the fistula is straight, otherwise search for it with a thin lead probe, as lead bends around twisted areas. If the fistula has many openings and cannot be found by probing, then irrigate it through one of the openings, as moisture will flow from one opening to another and cleanse it. Then probe it deeply until you know whether there is bone or nerve present, and how deep it is; ask the patient about their pain when you press your hand on it, and where they feel it most strongly. Once you truly know its location and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the locations I mentioned, then cut into it accordingly, removing the defect and corrupted flesh inside; then treat it until it is healed. If the fistula is very deep in the right place, then cut deeply into it as much as possible, then insert moistened probes dipped in acetic acid medicine up to the head of the fistula until the medicine corrodes any remaining excess tissue. Then apply healing ointments made from fresh meat until it is completely healed; if not, cauterize it as we have described. If the bone around the fistula is corrupted, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then cleanse until all corruption is removed, then treat external wounds until it is clean; and if it is not clean, and bowels resume as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: so uncover and seek until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus cleaned, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; if there is no other means than leaving it to nature. And if there are some small corrupted bones, and you can grasp them with tongs, then extract them using appropriate instruments, and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut through moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place something irritating on the wound to cause corruption, and leave it until the spot is corrupted all around the bones, and then they will come out more easily; and if it's a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, then just wait until the corruption has completely disappeared before restoring the wound. And if there is a large portion of decay reaching to the marrow of the bone, you must cut into it all the way up to the decayed part, and then treat it until it's sound again. And I will tell you about one case of fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that made matter come to the leg, causing it to swell with a large abscess that did not have an apparent cause. But foolish physicians operated on him so much that they caused the abscess to open, and they corrupted many materials, making it into a fistula, and there were many holes through which bowels and moisture from the body came out; and for two years many physicians attempted cures without any skilled hand at all until I was called in, and I saw his leg and the medicines that he was being treated with, and what flowed through the holes in large quantity. And the man's body became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those holes, then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which was rotted and perforated, with the corruption reaching to the bone within. I scraped away what appeared of the rotted bone, believing there was no other corruption besides that which I removed; and began to dress the wound with dissolving medicines for a long time, but it would not heal. Then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, finding that the corruption continued in the bone, which I scraped away, then removed it, and attempted to heal the place, but could not do so until I cut around about a palm's width of the bone, and drew it out entirely, then restored it with medicines. And it was soon healed and closed, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood was often needed, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he had good health with no harm or injury at all, neither in air nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it should be treated like this: take a linen cloth, and wrap it around the head of the exposed bone, and command someone to stretch it upwards; then take another thicker linen cloth than the first one, and tie it on top of the flesh that is above the bone, and pull the head so you can draw out the rotting flesh below, and uncover the flesh where you want it to be seen, so that the bone does not damage the flesh. And put a stick or a hot stone under the bone to move the rotting flesh away; and this should continue until you can see and feel the corruption, and still do it again once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a brand underneath, and then saw from one side to the other the corruption, and let the sawing be the length of the corruption of a span, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and saw the bone where it contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or foot, that is very difficult, but nevertheless you must examine this corrosion how it opens; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but let not the vein or nerve hinder you; and know that the tools for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance outside, and their thickness and their fineness, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its proper tool; and know that your work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you need according to what is right.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	When the head of the arm becomes inflamed due to internal causes or external injuries, and although you apply medicine for this corruption with medicinal treatments but it does not benefit at all, then you must cover that limb up to the point where the corruption began so that the patient escapes death either from this corruption or from the greater harm of losing the limb; and the sign is when the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and after the blackness spreads, these corruptions travel member by member throughout the body; so hurry to cover it up, and if it is due to the bite of venomous creatures such as sea scorptions or snakes and similar ones, cover from the head of the two fingers downwards but do not let it reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cover it at the joint so that corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cover it at the elbow; but if it passes beyond the elbow, then death is certain, and although there are powerful remedies available in large quantities, they serve no purpose; and likewise when corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover it above that joint; and if it reaches the foot itself, cover the entire foot; and if it spreads up the leg, cover at the knee joint; but if it is above the knee, there is nothing left to do except let the patient die. And the method of covering or bandaging the limb is as follows: tie it above and below with cloths, extend some ministers on one side of the lower tie and others on the other side of the upper tie, then cut away the flesh between the two ties using a wide spatula until the bone is exposed; then cover it with bandages or ointments, placing linen cloths on either side so that the ointment does not touch the healthy area and cause further injury and inflammation.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the area quickly, or apply powders that stop bleeding. Then return to your treatment until it is complete. Then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it heals; And I will tell you what happened to a man in great distress: He developed a blackness that seemed like burnt fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his right foot, spreading until it covered the whole foot. And when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off his foot and was healed. But long after, the corruption came again, this time on his hand, and he came to me. After cleansing his body, I applied things that would draw out the matter, but the corrosion did not stop. He then wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to do it, as I hoped to draw out the matter. But I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand he might die, for his strength was weak; And he despaired completely and returned to his land, hastening to cut off his hand, and was healed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Rarely does an abscess form in the flesh and remain so long that it collects a large amount of pus; then it becomes red and breaks open, the pus flows out, and the area remains empty like a vessel. The skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth and does not reach to the bone or nerve. Such an ailment is called 'sain' and not 'fistula'; but if it extends so deeply that it reaches the bone, it is then called 'fistula'. And the skin in this case is such that you should cut around that skin entirely, even when it is thin like a cloth.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin will rot and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it thus with a clyster: first look to see if the breast is large and the pus that flows from it has a foul odor. Then use the Egyptian medicine made like this: take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litargyros, and put them in a vessel on the fire until the medicine becomes red and thick like honey. Then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and insert it into the breast, closing the opening; let the medicine remain there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleaned out and free of corruption. Sometimes a clyster of water and ashes is used when this medicine is not present, using ashes from burnt vine wood, mixing them with water, and filtering it to use as a clyster until you know that the breast is well cleaned. And if the patient cannot tolerate this, nor the Egyptian medicine or the water and ashes, then use a clyster of water and honey with a little ground litargyros; or use a mixture of honey and wine, choosing honey with properties to cleanse and wash, and wine that makes the flesh harden. And when you have done this and believe that the breast is well cleansed, then use a clyster that promotes flesh growth using diachylon plaster mixed with rose oil and wine; or use other medicines and ointments whose properties I have discussed in the treatise on ointments. And if the opening of the breast is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it slightly with an iron tip and insert a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then close it except for the place where the clyster can enter. And if the opening that discharges pus is above, then cut below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowel is deeply prolapsed, do not allow any flesh to enter; and if you cannot grasp it below as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the bowel reaches its lowest point, for when the bowel is deep, no flesh should be allowed to enter. If you cannot grasp the bowel below as you see fit, arrange it so that it falls easily downward, leaving nothing of the bowel. Then take consolidating medicines to place on the skin, and spread them evenly on the linen cloth covering all the skin. Then cut into the breastbone a little larger than the first opening, for then spread soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the opening of the bowel to alleviate its prolapse. Do not remove the outer cloth but once after many days; and that which is on the opening of the breastbone, remove it often to remove the bowel, and note what comes from the bowel, whether it is venom or little or much, or digested, or undigested. Take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not. When your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see that it flows onto the opening of the bowel, then know that the breast has already healed, and the soundness approaches. Then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells with indigestion after many days, know that the breast is not improving.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle veins break open after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And there are men whose flesh grows late in healing their wounds, and those who heal quickly. And if the breast swells with indigestion after many days, know that the breast is not improving. And if the breast heals slowly, and is far away, apply drying medicines to it, such as diaphoretic ointment, which contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine. Take diaphoretic ointment and make it with rose oil and an equal amount of old wine; then cook it and use it. And if diaphoretic ointment is not present, do the same with honey increased in size, when you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and mix them with the honey while it is on the fire. Then dip a cloth in it and apply it to the breast, sometimes administering aristolochia longa and celestine roots, which are also like wheat and centaury flour. Use simples or composites: grind them and make powder, put it on the honey I mentioned earlier, and use it. And if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, know that the corruption has gone deep and has affected the bone or hard member or ligaments. Then treat the fistule as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the nail's abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Nail abscess is an infection that occurs under the nail of the thumb or big toe, or sometimes in other toes. If it is neglected and grows old, a black and swollen bump will appear, which may spread and consume the entire root of the nail, even reaching the bone, causing foul-smelling pain. The affected area becomes enlarged and has a yellow color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If the treatment does not work as we have described it and the cure is of no benefit, then you must cut off with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is very helpful if the bone and nail are healthy. If the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick and fester, then you must insert a hot iron under the nail where it touches the flesh, hold it in place and carefully cut away that part of the flesh with scissors or knife. Then apply burning and corrosive medicines to completely remove it. Afterwards, dress the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it off and draw out fire, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see both being corrupted, cut one of them at once as it is said before, then treat it until it heals; and if it is reddened and swollen, causing great pain, you must heal it first. Then cut the claw of the spina of the shoulder diagonally from above, making sure that the blade does not reach the flesh beneath the claw, for the patient would feel too much pain. And if this happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	Pain in the elbow of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some people's elbows are sometimes entirely fleshy and sometimes have bone spurs, and occasionally there is a claw, some of which grow at the root of the joint where their origin is in certain bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with a knot on the neck does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the neck sometimes moves; the girth of one who is fleshy is light, thus: cut him at his root with a broad scalpel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born from the root of the joint is difficult to treat: thus hold the cupper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born with a knot on the back of his neck, it is necessary that you first circumcise the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes on both cheeks together comes from birth, or from the closing of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Therefore you must cut away that swelling so that the cheeks regain their natural shape. Then place between them two damp cloths moistened in rose oil to prevent swelling, or place between them two thin pieces of lead until the area is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If at any time one of his hands swells with inflammation, then cut that swelling as it is necessary.
des vils	Of the evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, enveloping vessels full of melancholic excesses that come to many parts of the body; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you must administer him a purge for bile, and then wash him with holy water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you raise the vein and draw it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strong until the thick blood becomes subtilized, then hold the leg of the patient down from above the hip joint to below the knee; then cut the vein at one or two or three places, with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the virtue of the patient can withstand; and then tie it up, and command him to abstain from eating black bile; and recommence the evacuation and washing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, especially if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, then cut near the vein where the long hairs are at the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with an awl, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and it looks red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then place the probe underneath until it lifts the vein out of the skin, and then tie it to one ligature gently, then cut three fingers away on another place; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the probe as you have done before, and tie it to another ligature in the same way; then make another incision if necessary, then lift and cut at the two ends of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second incision; then extract it inch by inch until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, take a needle with strong double thread, tie it and pull it, and place it under the probe, turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have extracted it entirely, then place moist wool in wine and rose oil on the wound, and dress it until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut through it completely; and draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron tool with which one cuts the vein is curved and does not cut through it so as to open the vein; and it should be thickly curved for if it were too fine it would open the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the veins in general.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein enters the legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow and where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to putrefaction that comes under the skin, like how a serpent or worm enters inside the body, appearing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very great inflammation comes upon the leg, then the location changes and the vein begins to protrude forth like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, you must wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half to two inches long, fold it and tie it around the leg. Every time it points outwards, wrap the lead again and retie it. If it's too long, cut off a part, wrap the remainder and do not cut at its root, lest it enters the flesh and causes an abscess and decay in that place, leading to bad illness. For this reason, it must be treated bit by bit until it reaches its head, leaving nothing on the body. Sometimes this vein can be as long as five or ten palms; I once saw a man whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, insert one reed into the hole and pierce it to the bottom so that all of it comes out. Empty the matter inside and apply healing ointments to prevent decay for several days before treating it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens at the ankle joint or on the foot, where there are many perforations and it often bleeds; therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land 'cattle disease', because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and can be felt well as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it goes out, and leaves sores; and it is harmful due to corruption of some humors, like those that come from worms, serpents, leeches, and roundworms in the belly; and its malice is doubted, because when it goes through the body and reaches the head, it sometimes enters the eye and destroys it. This happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see one to cure and draw out, then it can only be done when it moves. Therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong, tight cord. Then cut into it and pull out the worm. If the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies. The greatest harm it causes is that it may run into the eye, as we have said. And if you see it coming near the eye or its head, press down firmly on the eyebrow below it, then cut into it and pull out the worm. The patient should also use bodily cleansing medications to dissolve harmful humors in the body, and avoid eating rotten foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "wakyr", and is a pain that comes into certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb. I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw something move like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, so much so that she came to have it in the other arm; then she told me that she was constantly turning around the body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she could move like this from limb to limb, for I had never seen such a disease behave in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had heard many times that pain could indeed move from one place to another, but I had not seen it happen as clearly as I saw it in this woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a thin body, with veins visible on the surface, and therefore this condition appeared more constrained; but those who are dislocated do not experience this reasonfully, for they have moist bodies and hidden veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain which we have described, then place a hot poultice above and below quickly, and then cut until that constrained wind is expelled from its place; cauterize the area; and if you cannot see it with your eyes, then treat it with those remedies that expel winds, such as fetid pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their shapes and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variations in their shape are such that there are those which have large points and small ones, barbed and welded; and those which have two angles, those with long shafts, and those with split ends. And those which strike any limb strike it in one of two ways: either at the start of the limb, like the head, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs, or along its length.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various ways; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.
