And the sign of death when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the scalp wound that is on the head becomes red, is when there is darkness before the eyes, swelling and straining and redness within them, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and mixing of the senses, vomiting of bile; and perhaps there will be without wound of the nostrils, or of the ears; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and from the wound flows white moisture like pigeon's milk, and also burned flesh comes out; and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the cure, and draw out the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow wound when it hits the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; sometimes the arrow moves like a bird's pulse, and black blood flows out, and chilliness and cold sweat come on, and fainting: then know for certain that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound in the lung is that foam comes out of the wound without pain, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the lung, it is near the ribs; and causes great shortness of breath and pain, and sighing; and all the shoulder members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, sometimes some undigested flesh may spout from the wound
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly and no excrement comes out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or extraction of the arrow
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and urine jumps out and blood comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary parts and spine of the back and hip and thigh and similar limbs, are saved according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you that happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened at the house of one that an arrow fell into his ear in the root of the nose; I probed it and drew it out on the other side under the fat of the ear without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And once I drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was bent back, and could only reach the tip facing the wood, and it was a large Turkish bow, all iron without ears; the eye was healed and no bad accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab-style arrow with ears; I grasped its feathers and pulled gently until I extracted it, and the Christian was freed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he extracted an arrow from the belly of a man who had fallen there and thought he would die. But after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. He cut into the arrow, twisted it, and pulled it out forcefully; there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man into whose back an arrow has fallen and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains inside him and does not change his natural condition nor cause harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And saw another man into whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound healed over it. He remained thus without suffering great pain, and there were many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And he extracted an arrow from the eye of one of the king's servants which had fallen there three days prior, and it was slightly inclined towards the right side. I was summoned to treat it afterwards.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I touched it with great care, and felt nothing; yet he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I applied to the wound an attractive and digestive plaster so that the wound would not swell up; then appeared the point of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster daily until the wound healed again. Then the patient remained like that for a long time until he felt the arrowhead one day near his neck; and he told me so
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound daily until it opened and I felt the head of the arrow which was stuck in place. Then I inserted the medicine into the opening of the wound with this medicine until the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and it took about four months for the inflammation to reduce so that I could insert the forceps into the wound, but the head could not be removed by pulling it from side to side. Therefore, I continued to use various tools carefully and skillfully, until one day I managed to grasp the arrowhead with well-made forceps according to its shape, as described at the end of this chapter; then I pulled it out and healed the wound
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient became entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	And I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I did not say, for books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare even small things, and find new work and new instruments based on what is present and lacking, descending upon strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows leave the limbs where they are stuck in two ways: either through the opening where they entered or through another part; and those which exit through the same place where they entered are called 'entrant' arrows, and sometimes they exit now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not exit now, leave it until the flesh around it rots and the wound heals; likewise, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for some days, moving it each day; then it will come out. If it does not, carefully cut around it with a scalpel until the surrounding area is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I mentioned appear to the patient: then do not pull it out but let it remain there for a few days, because if the arrow comes this far, death follows.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not go this far, and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then prepare to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very deeply like this and cannot be removed without further injury, then administer around the area tarares as I have told you; then heal the wound until it is clean.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in its place within the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the entire area; and if you can feel it, pull it out with some suitable instrument. And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins involved, then open the wound wider until it is large enough; and pull out the arrow if you can. And if there are barbs on the arrow to which it holds, cut away the flesh that has pierced both parts as much as you can, and then break off or bend the barbs of the arrow so that you can pull it out carefully, making sure not to break the arrowhead lest you cause greater injury.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, lay it until the place around is opened up, then draw it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, follow what we have said about its treatment in this chapter; and beware of cutting into nerve or vein, and devise how you can gently remove the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently. And place the patient as they were when the arrow struck them, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from another side, where something of it is visible or the skin is swollen there, cut open until you can grasp it with forceps, and then extract it; now it should come out easily.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out completely; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, remove it from the bone entirely; and if the bone breaks, and you see administration necessary, then administer the instrument carefully, so that the point of the arrow enters the socket of the instrument; and then force it out, and if the arrowhead is buried, push the instrument in with the point entering first, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is touched [embedded], then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can; then treat the wound as it ought to be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the thigh or belly or bladder or side and is nearby, and you can cut onto it, then do so; but be careful not to cut into the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; and care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is like a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to be placed at the tip of the arrow, as here is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the forceps for pushing and pulling out is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which blood is drawn there are 31, of which there are 16 at the head: namely, two temple veins that are behind the ears, called the two "herbich"; and two temporal arteries that are on the forehead; and two veins in the corners of the eyes, called "aspirations"; and one vein in the brow ridge; and one vein at the root of the nose; and two jugular veins in the neck; and two veins above the lips of the mouth, which are called "augulich"; and two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	Veins commonly spoken of are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, located on the right side and called by laymen 'vein of the head'; the median is named 'fossa', composed of the cephalic and basilica, and called by laymen 'vein of the heart'; the basilica is on the left side and called by laymen 'vein of the belly', located above the elbow and is the one from which we bleed openly, apparent on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The savatelle is the vein between the little finger and ring finger, with two branches; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one under the arch of the left calf, the second called 'saphena', located at the ankle on the right side; and the vein named 'nesse', found in the ankle of the other side. And in the other leg there are three more beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins behind the ears, if they are tied up with old bandages and made to bleed, are of such a quality that you should raise the patient's head and rub where the veins are with a rough cloth. Then have the patient strain their neck with a vise so that both veins appear behind the ears in two places at the back of the head: feel for them with your fingers, and where you feel the pulse underneath, pinch with your thumb; then take the lancet and insert it under the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand up along the entire vein and cut into both layers of skin so that blood flows out freely. Then bind and tie it tight until it stops bleeding; I have already spoken about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries located in the temples is useful for treating old migraines, dizziness, and customary eyestrain, as well as watery eye conditions. The quality of this bleeding is as follows: have the patient strain their neck so that both veins appear clearly; feel for the pulse underneath with your fingers and pinch with your thumb; then lift the heart upwards onto the vein with your index finger, insert the lancet underneath, raise the vein up and cut it as you did with the other two veins. Let blood flow according to what is necessary; then release the patient, place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; finally, bind it tightly and let it remain until it stops bleeding; we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	For the vein of the forehead's bloodletting is as beneficial as the cephalic in treating old facial illnesses, migraines, and redness; its qualities are such that the patient strains their neck by twisting until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "fossor", of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point upon the vein and strike with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to what you see fit. Then release the patient's neck and bind the vein until it ceases flowing and sometimes use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, do not allow the flame to be too strong; and cut the vein diagonally, as the bone is near by, and occasionally the thin flame may break.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins located in the arms aids the eyes, and helps with headaches, redness, and inflammation in the eye, as well as facial illnesses. And the qualities of their bloodletting are such that the patient strains their neck by twisting slightly, as before; then cut the vein diagonally, somewhat long and somewhat wide, for there is no flesh present.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they may break; then make it flow with blood, until you have enough, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The cauterization of the nose is useful for ague, and for sudden madness, and for facial illnesses, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic. The qualities of this cautery are: the patient stretches their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, and takes a long, subtle flame, and places it between the two nostrils in the space where the veins do not open well, and blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and let blood according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it heals quickly.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The cautery of the two temples helps with straining the eye, and the beginning of measles, and many illnesses, such as impetigo and corrosion, and herpes, and swelling. The qualities of this cautery are: the patient stretches their neck on both sides, as we have said; then the master stands on the head of the patient, who sits on a chair, then opens the vein slightly for a short distance, then let blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do the same on the other vein, then untie the bandage, and hold the veins gently so that the patient does not choke. Leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins in the lips aids in cooling the mouth, and prevents gum decay, lip cracks, and swellings around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the manner of performing this healing is as follows: Have the patient sit before you and constrain their neck as I have described; then turn up the lip, and look for the two veins, one on the right lip and one on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and the small black veins around them. Therefore, cut both of them, but if you do not recognize them or are uncertain, then cut the largest from each side, and also perform this operation on the two veins that are above and below them, for it is done in the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are beneath the tongue aids after the healing of the cephalic vein, and is used for narrowing the throat, and treating diseases of the eye and mouth. The manner of performing this healing is as follows: Have the patient sit between your hands before the sun, and have them lift their tongue, and look beneath each side for a black vein; then heal both of them, but do not cut too deeply, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm from which blood is commonly drawn are opened in two ways: either by pricking with a wide-bladed lancet or with an olive-shaped blade, sharp like a knife, and called "lancet"; and they are large and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mirror-like blade is very well-known, and it is wide as you can see
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to use the olive-shaped blade for opening the veins of the head that are full of thick, visible blood, and contain thick and turbid blood
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is used for opening fine veins where the blood is clear and yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bloodletting from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps those who are ill in the area below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the phlebotomist to bleed carefully and to beware of the artery that is beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he touches the artery and bleeding begins, then it must be staunched as I said; but the flame should not be scorching, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open visibly, then you must remove it and replace with another one; or you want some vein from it, or you cauterize in place of it the vein within the arm: it opens visibly; and touch the flame gently, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place for cauterization, first tie up the arm so that you may recognize the pulse; then mark the spot with a hot coal, and then untie the arm, and cut the vein with the flame gently; but be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something like urine issuing out high up, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and press your finger over the wound for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which happens often; if the bleeding does not stop, tie up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; and be cautious, and do not let him move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stanched, and it conquers you, and there are no physicians present, then cut the artery if it is open, for its head withdraws; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fig bark, cut it open, and take one half of it and tie it well until the next day. If the blood is stanched, that's good; if not, then heal it as we have said with powders that stanch blood. And these cauterizations do not harm in many cases due to the small size of the wound, nor does the power of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The sinew of the vein in its middle helps to draw blood from above and below it because it is composed of basilica and cephalic veins as we have said. And the surgeon must beware for the nerve underneath, and if it is pricked too deeply and the nerve swells, then the sinew may be injured and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens very often, but in some men it does not open due to its subtlety, so you must bind it with an absorbent bandage before you touch the nerve according to your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the temporal artery helps by drawing blood from the head and aids in sight; it is necessary to ligate it at its olive branch or mirror branch because this is the safest of all veins as it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the easiest place and not worry if one fails at first, and start again; sometimes the place may swell in some people when they fail at first, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the ligature depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about ligating is that a ligature is not done except to preserve health and prevent future illnesses; and it should be performed on one of the three veins found in the neck: the temporal, facial, and basilic veins. It should be done at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and in winter after meals when signs ofpletion appear. It should be done on the first or third day after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The leech administered to the sick has no fixed time, but when needed by day or night in all hours and at all times; nor should children be bled until they are fourteen years old, nor women pregnant except from the fourth month until seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should those who have passed sixty years not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, they should first cleanse the intestines with a light enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the principal members; nor should one bleed those who are too full of food or drunk, until they have sobered up, nor dropsical persons. And it is not proper to bleed after colic pains, vomiting, diarrhea, women's monthly flow, hard labor, watching, fasting, nor those entirely debilitated, either by injury or illness. Then subtly thin the humors with food and drink and medicines, if you have the skill; then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein on the left side around the third rib, as we have said; and that day avoid hard work, overeating, lust, and similar things. Be happy and cheerful, and let the bleeder be taller than the one being bled, and rub the arm twice or thrice, then pinch the flesh in the middle, for if it is too tight or thin, the blood cannot flow correctly; then moisten the blade with a little old oil, then place the thumb of the left hand on that vein below the rib where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not split or fail at the strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee like strings to the sinew, and some such are full of emptiness so that when one applies a flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and similarly many of these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be discerning in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first try, that's good; but if not, then begin again a little lower or higher suddenly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let him rest one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an ulcer will form there; nor should he enter a bath, then begin cutting again if it pleases him; and if the hole is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it is not flowing as much blood as you see, then strike with the fire directly into that hole itself; and open it suddenly before the place becomes swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not recommence the cutting, and put a little bit of oil ointment on it, for it lightens the body's blood and the oil has power in this place; and thus administer the oil ointment in each cut vein to stanch the flow of blood; and this same does troche and bowstring of sinew when it is placed on the spot; so subtlely does blood move and spread when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes up which happens many times, especially when it is not cut before except at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the spot an sponge moistened in water and heated somewhat, and hold it there for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein has stopped, and if it remains at the spot afterwards for some days with some blackness or greenness, then do not harm it; and if you see, put on some thing of aloe or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears an abscess and swelling at the base of the spine; therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the spot soft to the touch of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then do not place upon it any of the things that we have mentioned, for perhaps there is an ulcer without exit from the artery. But make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then treat with other remedies until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take from each person blood according to its quantity and color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red. And if you see it thick, let it become thinner. And if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And one who is full and robust and needs bloodletting should be given a larger wound and have wide-flared flames. But one who is weak should be treated conversely: they should be bled gently and often, cutting across rather than puncturing; this method of bleeding prevents excessive blood loss and damage to nerves, and is better than long or deep cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	**And for one whose body fails at digestion, they should give soft bread in the juice of pomegranates; if heated, let them bleed three or four times. And if cold by nature, let them eat before digestion soft bread in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.**
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	**And if he loses his digestion after much bloodletting, then it is necessary that he inhale broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.**
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	**And if he wishes to evacuate some bile and digest another time, then when weakened by much digestion, let him digest little by little, according to the quantity of his continuous strength.**
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	**And whoever wishes to evacuate some bile after the first digestion, and has a strong body, let him digest seven hours after the first digestion, or after the ninth hour.**
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to wash on another day, they must wash on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And since there is much blood inside the body that has already heated up and causes fever; thus it is necessary to draw out a large quantity of it, and widen the hole until it resembles a coin; then, when you have prepared all the conditions for washing, place your hand on the pulse while he washes, so that no blood comes in place of water, which happens often if the washer is negligent. But do not press strongly if you want to loosen the arm and make blood come out a second time, especially when the hole is closed; nor should one stretch out the arm hastily if it is curved, for this would be harmful; but let him wash until the second washing is done; or else prick with the tip of the flame until the frozen blood comes out through the vein's hole; then place a bit of wool dipped in water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess quiets.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so in that same vein or another vein or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is used instead of the vein near the head because it is more convenient.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is thus: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the veins appear red. Then tie it loosely so that the vein appears well. Now draw blood perpendicularly, not wide nor long; and make the puncture large. Draw blood close to the joint of the hand. If no blood comes out, immerse the hand again in warm water, allowing the blood to flow into the water until you have enough. But if it is summer time, do not immerse the hand again in warm water, for bloodletting is done more often in winter than in summer. The vein of the arm is safer to draw from than any other veins because there are no arteries nor nerves present.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the salvation of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it should be applied: constrain the hand, and immerse in warm water until the vein swells so that it can be seen; and if the vein is crossed, and if you cut it entirely across, it will not cause any harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves lie beneath all bare of flesh, and then place the hand back into warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound so that it can exit.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And once you have removed as much blood as is necessary, then place oil and a wick on the vein to quickly cauterize it, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and perform all as I have told you concerning the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the sophena is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the womb, retention of menses, and diseases of the kidneys, thighs, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its heating is that the patient places their foot in warm water, and rubs on the vein until it reddens, and ties above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and many veins go from there up the leg; therefore heal where the largest vein or at the ankle, which matters more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the leg, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut across like when cutting meat; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out, then place the foot back in the water, and allow the vein to empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the veinisser fails the first time, then begin again a little higher up, for the place is stained; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise to the sinew of the other leg evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its healing is useful for hot hip pain.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this healing is that when the patient enters into the bath and presses down on the ankle with four fingers in twisting, otherwise the vein will not open. And if it opens, then let the blood flow in all ways you can, and across. It is better to wipe it away, for the place is dry and the blood flows copiously from many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then let some blood flow from one of those veins that opens at the back of the foot, near the little toe, and beware of nerves. And drain as much blood as you can see, then untie the bandage and put cotton on it and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting by cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or clay, or glass. And cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without striking is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire. And cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is performed on fourteen parts of the body, namely one at the top of the head; another on the neck; two on both sides of the neck; one under the chin; two on the shoulders; two on the buttocks; two on the arms; two on the legs; and two on the ankles. This cupping does not draw much blood but only from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, so it does not weaken the body as much as bloodletting from a vein. It is not necessary to administer it with or without fire in any disease caused bypletion, unless the whole body needs to be emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary to ventose due to illness or habit, we will bleed them each hour at the beginning or end of the month, and also in between and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to ventose, have a heavy head. And there are those who findpletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes. And there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an swollen tongue, and vomit blood. And there are those who dream, and see by their blood, wounds and dead people and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is mid-month, we tell them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the temple helps with headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to be done after evacuating the whole body; this bloodletting is in place of cephalic bloodletting, and those who are of cold complexion or have dizziness should not use it, as it does great harm to them. And so elders and those with cold-headed illnesses should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often cured thereby become forgetful; therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower out of fear of relapse.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping at the neck is beneficial for treating ailments of the head and stomach, as well as for constipation, colic, andpletion. However, it must be applied carefully, as too strong a hold can cause relapse in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the second ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, ophthalmia, migraine, constriction, and toothache. It also aids in treating stomach ailments; however, instruct the practitioner to press gently when applying it, so as not to damage the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gingivitis, and similar conditions affecting the mouth. It also aids in treating cracked lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Wind-evil of the shoulders helps against an illness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosation of the ribs is as useful as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and command the surgeon not to dig too deeply, for the spot is bare of flesh, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the buttock is useful for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large and made of brass so that it can draw well; but if it were delicate, it might break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs draw openly because they attract blood from the whole body and are useful for old pains in the loins, sciatica, and bladder problems, and improve circulation; they are placed on two thighs and two ankles, but they also weaken the body after prolonged use and cause dizziness in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is as follows: first place it empty, and suck temperately, and put it on quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see where it becomes red and swollen, and appear the redness of blood; then stop, and remove the cups, and be careful in the positioning of the body, for there are many who have thick flesh and clear pores: thus one should strike only once, and make large wounds, but not too deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, then one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood little by little, it suffices to do so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we desire much blood, then we recommence often; and if the blood is dense, strike deeply, and the end will be when the heart pierces suddenly. And it behooves those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with refining and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil or sweet almond oil or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil or lily oil or camomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of almonds, or of balsamite, or oil of anise, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one's skin is tender and has large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcellain, or other similar ones.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have too much moisture should rise from bed with myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or water of succory, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones; and they should not be cupped before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one or two hours later; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he wash himself when he must be cupped and when he is cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware those who are excessively choleric, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed; they should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar foods; and eat pigeons and castrated hare meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey and medium-scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat peacock meat, pigeons, small birds, and chickens; and on the day they expect to have wind, they should drink more than eat; and some men should sometimes be given treacle or muscat before the ventosication, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members; and let the blood be subtilized, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are placed without cauterizing are those placed on the liver and on the kidneys, and on podagry, and on the stomach, abdomen, back, and buttocks, for these limbs cannot withstand cauterization and it is only done to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on the breasts when there is inflammation; to remove viscosity from the limb, as we place cups on the stomach and abdomen to reduce the limb; and it relieves pain where there is oppression or stone, perhaps by its attractive power drawing off the oppression or moving the stone from its place; and similarly it acts when placed on the liver and kidneys when there is retained wind, and these cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cup with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two mouths of half a palm's width and depth, with a small hole on each side around the middle, like that for inserting a needle, and they are made of brass, smooth in front so they do not cut the patient when placed on the limb; and there is a transverse bar of brass or iron in the middle to hold a wick candle, and there should be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the size of those who use them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of old people, and those of thin people differ from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping glass on the limb thus: light the candle wick made of wax or linen, and insert it into the glass through the transverse bar inside the glass so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass and does not burn the patient; then place the glass on the limb with both mouths over the holes we mentioned earlier, so that when you wish, the steam can escape, and remove the glass; and take the wick as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure used for the disease of pleurisy with acute fever, it has neither tube nor hole, and is not filled with fire unless it is full of air, and is placed only on the member; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without heat, cupping is used only in members where one cannot place cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; also in fleshless locations, like the toes or nails, and other similar ones. The quality of the user is that when you find leeches that are in clear, sweet waters without any injury, take them; put them for a night in sweet water until they become accustomed, having nothing in their bellies; then clean the vein and the cup, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the leeches on top. And when they become full and fall off, if it is a location where one can place a cupping glass, place one there, for this is very beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not so, then lift the joint gently, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the joint bleeds too much after the body of the wound, wet a linen cloth in cold water and put it on until the bleeding stops; and if the blood increases, put ground vitriol or salt, etc., until it stops flowing; or you put half a handful of peeled beans on the joint and let them sit until they swell at the joint, now it will stop flowing; and if you need more of this, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds will not take, then rub fresh blood on the joint, or stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will swell; and when you see that they are full, sprinkle some powder of aloe and bulrushes crushed together, or ashes, now they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
