Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that foolish physicians neglect this chapter because they have never seen any of the ancient books or letters about it. Because of this, medical knowledge is lacking in our land, for I found no good practitioners here; and I know nothing except through the knowledge gained from the ancient books which I have studied so much that I have practiced medicine through experiment and practice. In this chapter, I have described what is contained therein and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the forms of instruments that are required, as I did in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the essence of the words and chapters where the wise man focuses his attention and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or concussion comes upon any individual, then you must hasten to heat the patient on both sides if nothing prevents you from doing so entirely, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; unless the time is very hot or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say cold drinks, and bird meat and venison, and do not drink wine nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill oneself too full with foods that fill the veins with blood until you doubt a hot abscess or an expansion of matter in the limb. Then return the patient to his first government which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, then you must nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, pancakes of veal, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at such nourishment movement repeats quickly, often breaking bones.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and feeble do not heal well nor unite according to their nature due to weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but there is no treatment, reset on the broken bone large splints which support and join the limb together until it becomes strong again; and do not shorten any part of its work, and therefore it is necessary to nourish them with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go upwards, and others that pierce, like cutting a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if fracture with wound, and fracture is through a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own device, and its proper instrument in restoration, according to how the memory comes back into its place; and bone fracture is known by the twisted place, and is evident by lack of sound, and heard when pressed with the hand; but if there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting, or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it with your hand, but put on medicines that follow below, and then gently hold it in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that fractures which go into the air are those where the two parts are disjoined; you must bring them together evenly so that no inflammation comes; and if inflammation does come, let it be for some days until it is appeased; then set the bone in its proper place gently and smoothly, knowing that the restoration of this one will be easier than those with pieces; then hold it as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in pieces, then splint it with two parts, if it's a hand or foot, or with your hand if it's a small member, or with two ropes, or one rope and your hand; And place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are aligned, you straighten it with all your strength, and ensure that through your work no injury nor pain comes to the patient; And join the two ends of the bones together in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems not to be right; Then straighten it nicely, and do not pull too hard, nor press so that by your work heat and stiffness come to the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, instruct the patient well that he not move it, neither in waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor any other way; And ensure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	When he feels any pain, it is not yet complete, and you must put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and make sure that he is properly placed so that there are no twists when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs differ in smallness, size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	But there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: they should be wrapped in soft, thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and calves, should be wrapped in a wide, hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb and squeeze it evenly from all sides so there is no gap; then tie it around with light pads, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand somewhat on the whole bandage, then go up above the break and tighten less so that the break can open a little; and soften the bandage bit by bit until you grasp most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again around the broken area; then return to the part below the break and tighten moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above; then put pads of linen or cloth between the bandages so that they are all even, then tie everything up with a sling, and then place your well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then apply a warm compress to soothe the abscess and reduce the swelling, leaving it on for several days; then tie it tightly with bandages made of half of a thick cane split lengthwise, or wood from which wedges are made, or palm fronds, shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the bandage that is placed on the fracture must be a little thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or length. Then tie it tightly over the bandages, just as you did on the first layer of the break; tie again evenly, but not too tight nor too loose; and the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen. For if the threads are thick, like those foolish people who make their bandages from twisted hemp ropes, it is a great mistake; for the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each layer.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of stones after the extraction in clean places, then place underneath them linseed poultices, or woolen bandages, so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with breaking and the bone is broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that one should not extract all stones from the limbs broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, one should not insert stones before five or seven days, or more according to the certainty of an abscess happening; and here is the manner of ancient plasters for restoring breakage, dislocation, and torsion: Take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg whites, and make this mixture neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common manner of the plaster restoring breakage in many ways, and especially for women and young children, as it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for plaster restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take storax and ladanum and mallow and asafetida and gum arabic and nard, each three drachms; myrrh and aloes, each five drachms; aloe wood nine drachms; and grind them into powder, and mix with egg white. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for plaster good for twists: take nard and vismalva, each ten drachms; myrrh and aloes, each nine drachms; acacia six drachms; bolus armeniacum ten drachms, and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for plaster for joints and for bones out of their places, and eases the pain occurring, and stops the bone growth, and fracture: take new linen, and soak it in hot water and cooked oil, and put on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore (the joint), but it is good for soothing a hot boil, and it removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster to restore broken bones: Take dried fig leaves and earth pear leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of woodbine, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour (each one part); grind and mix with wine. If the limb is warm, mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it as a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger plaster than the first one for when a hard abscess comes to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of woodbine, linseed, balm, melilot, sansuce, violet and camomile flowers (each one part); grind and mix with salt water, fresh water or wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book not to apply anything to a broken limb for restoration except cerate made of wax and oil alone. He also says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems according to Galen that one should apply dry and slightly warm substances to a broken limb for restoration, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method for plasters that is good for injury and pain: take mastic and chopped human hair or chicken feathers, and gum tragacanth, and mix them together equally, grind them into a paste, and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the plaster a little later, and ensure that the patient feels no pain nor has any movement of the bone from its place; if not, do not remove it for several days. But if pain or itching comes to the area, with heat or swelling, act quickly, remove the plaster, and wipe off the plaster gently; then take a light cloth and wet sea sponge, dip it in water, and lift up the affected area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool moistened with rosewater or oil of roses to the bandage, tying it tightly until you are sure there is a warm wound; and when the inflammation has subsided and the pain is gone, begin again the gentle treatment, applying a little plaster but not too tightly as before. Continue this until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen has all gone away, and you need plaster and bandages, then recommence it, just as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, then do not untie it until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture becomes apparent, and the joining of the flesh approaches; then tighten it more than before, and the swelling increases its flesh, as I have said earlier. And if you see that the place dries too much than is needed, know that nourishment cannot come there; therefore give then warm water to drink, every time you untie it, and this should be done every third day, and slacken a little the bandage. By this way, nourishment comes to the limb, and quickly corrects what foolish doctors do, who reset the limb crookedly: that is wicked, and such works are fearful, and I see nothing else but leave it and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various ways bones can break
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways bones can break and diverse shapes, and their causes differ; for there are breaks caused by the impact of a sword, where the neck bone shatters all the way down to the face that is beneath the bone, as if it were wood. And thus this type of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts across the bone without piercing it, this type of break is called "absolute"; and both of these breaks cause wounds that are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow from behind, or a split due to falling on stone or hitting it with the head, or from falling onto stones or similar events.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or is on top of it, this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that enters the bone as fine as a hair, and the fracture is small. This break is called "capillary"; And if there is a wound made by striking with stone or falling, which pushes the bone fragment inward like blacksmiths do when they strike on anvil, then the stone gets inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in the head, such as children's heads; and it occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are dislocated like stars; and I will speak about this in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by their depression and by probing them, and by the rotted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is known because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed with incense, the fracture opens black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, beware of accidents that might affect the patient. If you observe any bad symptoms such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, rigidity, swelling, fever with chills, and eyes projecting and turning red, among other similar dispositions, then healing cannot take place without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any frightening accidents, and you hope for a good outcome, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded first comes to you, especially in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the wound that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the flesh beneath the bone becomes corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the flesh that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the broken part thus: and take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover upon the bone in all ways that you can, and gently upon the appearance of the wound, and if blood flows or a boil appears, help him as it is needed, and fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the boil is appeased, and be assured of no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut narrowly before it, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is thus: you should have several diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, sharp-pointed, and made of fine iron; perform them easily, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, you must pierce around it before applying incisions with trepanations, not too deep that they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull; each should have a guard or ring above the point to prevent the point from protruding through the bone. You should have several so that each fits properly on the edge of the bone, so you have trepans for all heads; this is the shape of the three types of trepans:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To pierce around the broken bone: place the trepan on the bone and twist with both hands until you feel that the bone is pierced. Then move the trepan a little further along and repeat all around, then carefully cut away the space between the holes using scissors, doing so gently so as not to damage the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cleaned it, then you must reset the sharp edge that remains from the bone to all other tools resembling an inciser, but it must be more thin and more subtle than the other incisors; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with the instruments. Then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of work is that which Galien speaks of, which is hotter; he recommends it strongly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture appears movable, so that once you have uncovered this part, you will place under the head of this lenticular inciser, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut on one side, and the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone. Then strike gently with a small hammer, so that you easily break the bone all around, and beware of the membrane underneath; if it is adherent to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is only cut on top, with small pieces present, then you must remove this asperity, and scrape away the scales using a fine file of which you should have various quantities to provide the most suitable in each case according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use coarse files initially, then proceed with finer ones, until it is well smoothed out.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other types of capillary and subtle fracture cuts, you must adapt according to its direction; this is something not answered by one who has not devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sinew is exposed, then you must take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound. Then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as lightly as possible so you do not weigh down the sinew, then apply another lien on top, and do not tie it too tightly except to merely hold the cloth against the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the inflammation is eased, then remove it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, frankincense powder, incense powder, aristologist, and similar things. Make a powder of these ingredients and place it on the wound, and always apply medicaments without biting (i.e., do not use corrosive substances). Ensure that the wound is always clean, leaving no ointment or allowing bowels to accumulate on the brain's skin, for when bowels gather on the brain's skin, they corrupt and fester, causing great harm to the patient. For when one places something corrosive on the sinew, it necroses from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be cautious if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, so it is doubtful whether there is doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no blackness comes out except because of the medicine that was applied, which has such power, then you should take one part honey and three parts rose oil and mix them with one drachm of gum, and place it on the sore; then cure it according to its manner of curing until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the knee joint above are broken, or one by itself, because these are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break unless forced or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should place your little finger in the hole of the knee joint and put the break evenly against it with your index finger behind, until the knee returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the thigh cannot come to its place, then you must align it at the head of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, then do likewise; and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then apply to the head of the thigh bandages of linen cloths.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And if you bind one on another part where the fracture is; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the thigh.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one must wet the bandages in butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but rather the bandages should be moistened with a mixture of ground ivy and powdered mallow seed; then leave the bandage on until the bone is solid and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one applies goose feathers in place of tents, and if the swelling is hot, it holds the fracture in place, and let the patient blow through them.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil comes near while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a little of diacereum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil does not come near, then put a plaster made of ground mustard seed and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk; then place light bandages over it, without binding tightly. And if the fracture is small but shattered into many pieces, extract them with suitable tools, then sew up the break and treat the wound as usual with plasters and salves; and if there is no wound inside the joint, then treat it with tents, placing splints of lead until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below without any wound appearing, and the fracture is only slight with no more than two breaks, which can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your left index fingers into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left jawbone, insert your right index finger, then gently press the fracture inward with one hand while holding it even with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is displaced posteriorly in two places, you should provide traction of both sides until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth or fracture occurs, tie them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk; then place cerote on the broken jawbone and cover it with a double cloth. Place a well-made splint or an equal piece of leather on top, long and wide according to the jawbone, and fasten it at the angle where you can reach it. Instruct the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes shape, release it on the third day, and then put back what has been dislocated in its proper place; and apply a poultice of powder from the mill with plenty of eggs or sesame flour after removing the grease; and cover the poultice with light linen, and if the poultice heals and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling occurs from an abscess, apply what we have said many times
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, make sure no piece of bone has been broken off; carefully remove it with instruments suitable for that
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have removed all these pieces and none remain, sew the wound shut if it is wide, and apply one of the appropriate poultices to encourage healing until it is sound.
de la forcele	Of the cautery
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The cautery often breaks in front of the shoulder-blade and such breakage occurs in three ways: where it is broken but not dislocated in two places with pieces resulting in the easiest restoration; or where there is breakage along with wounding.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work of this is when there is breakage without wounding: you should have two assistants so that one holds the shoulder where the cautery has broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part. Then place your hands equally on either side of the break so that its shape is as it should be, with neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place under the shoulder of the patient a round bolster made of cloth or wool, its size according to your needs. Then lift and move the cautery, pressing the bolster against your hand so that you may set the break evenly as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder blade at its front, because it comes from deep within, then the patient should lie on his back, place a pillow under his shoulder, and the assistant press down on the shoulder so that the bone of the shoulder blade is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your two hands. If you find it difficult to do so, then cut across it. Remove the fragments gently. And if the bone cannot meet due to any obstacle, then make an incision on one of the incissors that you have; but place this tool under the shoulder blade as a warning.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it should look like a spoon and not be sharp, and be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work. And it should have two heads, one wide and the other narrow, just like the shape of the wound you made when you removed the bones. And once you are sure that there is hot inflammation, close the wound. But if the wound is small or you doubt there is hot inflammation, then fill the wound with lint and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an ulcer forms there, then soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and place it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The reduction of a bone fracture when it is without wounds and incisions is that you put on the plaster made from the flour of millet and eggshells, and place light pads on top, and put a pillow underneath the armpit if needed; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put the doubled cloth on top of the pads and the plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the splint on the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and tighten each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break firmly, and you see clearly that the splint does not move over the broken bone, then rewet it every day, and when the wrapping loosens, then tighten it; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow underneath the armpit to lift the shoulder up; thus lighten the break by easing the tension of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck if no harm comes from it, for up to twenty days; then restart the plastering if needed, and tighten and leave it like that until it is healed; and it is healed in twenty-eight days at most, and fewer in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder bone is broken or moved from its proper place, and it cannot be felt except by touch; then apply it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways; then put on the spot powder of wheat with plenty of egg yolk, and light bandages, and cover it with a double cloth; then put over it a wide and thin compress, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the compress in some part of the shoulder, fill that hair with linen bandages so that the compress lies evenly; and then bind it all firmly with a large bandage so that the compress does not move from its place, and check the binding each day; and every time it loosens, tighten it, and keep the compress even if it has moved from its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be reset in 20 or 25 days, And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure of it, for this is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out, and points under the heart, so it pushes up, and causes pain, do as we have said in the breaking of the arm regarding quieting hot inflammation.
de la brisure dou pis	And about the fracture of the arm
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The arm is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the forearm.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it leans downwards, and the patient feels great pain, faintness, and shivering, and sometimes vomits blood; and the cheekbones appear through the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and they put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of both sides with their hands, gently putting them even in all ways possible until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and dressings above the delicate splint made of salt or other light wood, and wrap it in one cloth, tying it onto the broken bone so that it does not move; and tie the knot around the back, tightening it properly, and tighten every hour until the swelling decreases; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or inflammation, then hurry up and loosen it, remove the bandage, and address what has come from ways of treatment; then renew the bandage, tightening it until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures occur mainly in large bones behind the back and at the head inside, and ribs break only because they are smooth; this is clearly felt upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the splint, and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is inclined inward, then the patient feels very great pain and sharpness like pleurisy because the bone pierces the membrane; the patient also has difficulty breathing, coughs violently, vomits much blood, and this is a sign of severe illness, as the ancients said.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly to push the fracture back into place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless an abscess has formed if it was present.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes to this, then cure it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one puts cupping glasses on the spot to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cupping glass will draw out the excesses to the place due to weakness of constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the spot with wet wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the bandage even, then treat it with the cure for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt about the patient, then one must cut onto the spot of the broken rib, and place something underneath to guard the sac; and then one must trim the bone, gently pull it out, and afterwards sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess appears suddenly, then place cloths soaked in rose oil on it, and apply heat to the affected area; treat the area according to what is appropriate for an abscess, and keep it constantly warm on its side until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	A fracture of the neck bones does not occur often, and rarely is it dislocated; and likewise with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if you see their hands are softened, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or extend them; and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases; and if they move and feel when the joints are constrained or pricked, know that the articulation of the bone is saved, and that the patient can be cured with care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is healthy or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if accidents have occurred which are in the hands, and windiness and evacuation occur without will; and when one has slept on their belly, so does evacuation occur without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he sleeps on his back and wishes to turn over, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Such are those who are mortal: do not labor in their care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you examine whether there is a hot abscess, and if so, apply rose oil or goose grease oil to it until it is appeased. Then place one of the comforting and drying emplasters on it, and bind it with linen, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, then bind tightly over the heart; remove the bone, then approximate the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then treat with ointment until it is healed. And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', place your left hand's pouch there and make it equal to the other hand by force, then apply splints and bandages if needed; then bind tightly, and if there are dislocated bones, cut them off, remove them, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the thighbone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a little diminution of movement at the hip; and it cuts with pain, declines toward the knee, and comes to the patient with pain and numbness, and swells where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the reduction is thus: you stretch your hand upwards until you are above the fracture; and know what is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture evenly, until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their belly so that the reduction of that fracture may be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have set it evenly, then place the splint on top, followed by a wooden or bone roller, and compress the fracture so that it does not move; and place the support under the ribs so that the binding is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an inflammation occurs there, do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided, and then apply what we have mentioned before; and then return to the reduction, compressing it as is necessary if there are no bad complications; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder-blade is that which lies between the rib-cage and the head of the shoulder; if it is broken, it should be reset in one of two ways. One way is to take a stick as thick as your thumb, shaped thus:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads of the stick with two cords and raise them up. Then have the patient sit on a seat. Then place the broken arm on the stick so that it comes to the shoulder-blade, and fits into a curve in the wood. Then place something heavy or let the assistant pull downwards. Then the physician should hold both sides of the break evenly with his hands until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to have the patient sit on his haunches. Then let him hold his hand at his neck. Then instruct two assistants: one to pull what is above the break with both hands, and the other to pull what is below it with all their strength, each stretching in his direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then hold the ligaments beneath and above the fracture, and extend each of the helpers to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place one ligament beneath the angle and another towards the elbow beneath the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the elbow, then you must gently place the ligature without effort until the fracture is even on its place and on the elbow; then set the fracture evenly as it should be and hold it steady in case any abscess occurs.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess occurs, do not hold the ligature for seven days and place a moistened cloth in oil of roses until the abscess is appeased; then hold it steady, and the method to hold it steady is: place the bandage on the fracture, bring the arm onto the shoulder, place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest, place the cloth on the shoulder and the arm, and pull towards the shoulder so that the arm is in its proper position unless something prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use wedges and place a larger and stronger wedge on the break than the others, leaving two fingers' width between each wedge. Each wedge should be large enough to extend three fingers beyond the break on both sides; then press on the wedges as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, firmly but without straining the limbs apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the wedges' base and their pressure as we have said in the wound where you reset the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it alone for seven days as we have said; then check each day whether any itching or swelling occurs at the site where the ligature cannot reach the limb due to its being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it does not heal, as we have said
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not untie the ligature until three days or more have passed, and have the patient lie on their back with their hands on their stomach. Place one cushion filled evenly with wool under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night to ensure that the broken limb's alignment does not change nor the ligatures become loose. Then heal it through the power of medicine, and give them the food we have mentioned earlier, in such a way that at first it is subtle, then gradually thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be immobilized for 40 days after which one should remove them, administer baths and ointment medications to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is severe and stuck in place, it must remain immobilized for 50 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	Regarding the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the 'fuscile', one of which is small and guides the thumb, while the other is large and situated below towards the little finger. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, or sometimes only the small one, but occasionally both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bone is broken, healing is easy and recovery swift. However, when the large bone is broken, healing is difficult and more painful than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently pulled out straight and set evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large hip joint, then it must be pulled harder; and stretch him over the pillow, and hold your hand pouch higher than the others, and let the little finger hang lower than the other fingers, and have the patient lie crossed upon himself, and place the pillow higher before him so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand or elbow, and another minister at the other end above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the physician puts it back in place according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there is fragmentation in the break, then place each piece back in its proper place, and if any fragment is too small to grasp with forceps, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut around it and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound accompanying the fracture, I spoke about that in the separate chapter on wounds; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if, at the beginning of restoration, boils appear, then apply a bandage made of cerote cloth softened with rose oil and white wax, ensuring it is neither too hard nor too soft. Bind the bandage gently until the boil subsides.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote and apply a plaster made of millstone powder mixed with abundant egg white. Next, place the splints, ensuring that the main splint is always stronger and slightly wider than the others. Know that there should be six splints on the arm in various arrangements: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and bind more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, gradually decreasing tension as you move away from it, as I said at the beginning of this chapter. And let the bandages on the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or harsh; and let the thread used for binding be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.
