And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wash the limb with hot water until that itching is appeased; and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the bandaging, and if the joint is loosened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, so treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it happens that the bandaging cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should soften it a little and leave it thus for some days until the bandaging reaches, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not unbind it for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And otherwise, then place the hands around the neck, and make them even, and beware of movement and dislocation, and sleep on the back; and know that this dislocation can be restored in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on our two hands there are few breaks, and there only comes much bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should hold his arms crossed, and sit upright before him evenly; then place his hand on the table extended, and the minister stretches the broken bones, and the master aligns them until they are well joined; and places the plaster and bandages if there is no abscess, then puts a splint according to the size of the area; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the edge around the belly of the palm, then make a splint of bandages and instruct the patient to bind it to their broken palm; then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be made of soft wood as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the end, you should place one splint above and another below in the sole such that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and make the tie tight between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs at any of our fingers, especially if it is the thumb, set it straight as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit, place a small upright splint to lift the fracture so that it does not move. And if the fracture is in another finger, such as the index or one of the others, set it straight, and tie it with the healthy finger that follows; either tie them all together at once, whichever way works best, or place a splint on top like you would with the thumb. Take care with the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and treat those who come to it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it is clear when it turns front to back; and the treatment for this is to bind one lien above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each minister extends their bandage to their side evenly; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hip, one bandage should be toward the thigh, and the other bandages below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is near the knee, then one bandage should be by the knee, and its extension below; then the surgeon places the bone evenly with both hands so that it returns to its natural shape, and then applies the splint and binding, especially if inflammation does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot inflammation, leave it to cool, then return to your work and treatment; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a hard doubled bandage, two or three layers thick, and hold it in place with splints; then turn the leg so that the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the hip and the leg below the knee, bringing the ends up; then wrap the bandage over the leg and hip again, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the shinbone; then fill the space between the leg and hip with soft cloths to ensure even pressure, then begin tying tightly three or four times around the fracture; as you go higher up the fracture, tie less tightly; then reach for the two ends of thread that you inserted between the leg and hip, tie them together over the splints placed above; then return down to the bottom end of the thread until you reach the foot; and tie it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus until no swelling, inflammation or other similar condition appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it occurs, then dislocate it, and realign what has moved, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they must be removed if possible; and if not, then the place must be split open, and burned with fire. And treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone breaks in this manner when nails are inserted into it, such as in the shoulder or arm; nevertheless, in such restoration, the limb does not become deformed.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is restored in about 40 days, or a bit less or more, according to the various constitutions of individuals.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the cruciate ligament of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the cruciate ligament of the knee there is little breakage, but it often stretches.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is merely a split or hole, which happens in every wound, and without wound, and this is well-known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: put what is round on its two sides until it is assembled and can move; then place the bandage, and if you need one, add a rounded pin, and tighten as necessary; then review all the positions that we have described in other breaks, such as a hot abscess and similar things; apply to each accident whatever is needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that the leg has two bones, of which one is rightly called «crus» and the other «tibia»; and all kinds of breaks come to it as they do to the arm, and for this reason its restoration is done in the same way as that of the arm, and the work is entirely the same. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible; and it turns inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply traction, set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the break is ugly with many pieces, make the traction lighter and gentler; and lift according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of forked wood that embrace the leg on both sides, their length from the knee downwards. Then wrap them in two places with bandages above and below, tie them in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, which is good. Some add one support of wood along the length of the leg for further protection, and place the leg at rest to prevent movement. This is particularly done if there is a wound at the break. Move the leg each day to check for heat or other signs of inflammation. Continue the treatment until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but sometimes a break occurs in the bones of the foot and in the toes; only shaking happens in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breakage in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding over each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then put your foot on theirs where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply a splint and compresses, and place a small table with two heads under the belly of the foot, then bind it tightly, and wrap it with bandages and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even and healed.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, restore them as we have said for the toes of the hand; then put a splint on the broken toe according to its length and make it slightly wider, then place the table I mentioned under the foot and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three or more broken toes, place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table under the foot; let them stand upright at the head of the table so that they extend well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, which we have discussed; and treat each injury as it ought.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, have her sit with her legs apart, then lean her towards the back part and hold her from behind. Fill the hollow of her nature with cotton, as thick as one's fist, then raise the woman slowly, little by little, until the cotton reaches the entrance of her nature and the bone returns to its place. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has done so, replace it. Do this for about seven days or thereabouts: the fracture will be healed. If you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube to the opening, and blow into the tube until the bladder is full inside her nature. Then fill her with cotton and leave it like that for some days until she is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from those who set their study and practice on it, and hear my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	But breaking signifies in many cases the right path to restoration: therefore follow it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take a goose quill and insert it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it and let it remain for three days or so until it is healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	with wounding break
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with wounding, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be healed immediately, so that the healing which we have said may testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then apply a dressing of vitriol, if you have nothing else; then begin to reset the break at that same hour or day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess occurs there, let the restoration continue until the ninth day, so that the abscess may be healed; and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is visible breaking over the uncovered heart, then it is necessary that you put it back in place lightly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear easy to make equal with your hands, then reset it with this iron tool, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width should match the size of the wound; and the smith must shape it into three or four sides, according to what is needed in each treatment of a break; and let it be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend during compression on the limb at your work; and it should be pointed in front and thick in the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche,' which means the curved head should be placed on the visible bone of the joint; then push it back once until it returns to its original position, and align them evenly.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is delicate, and the tool cannot grip the bone well, then you must cut off the head of the bone so that the tool can grasp it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then with an appropriate tool such as a saw or scalpel, cut carefully and cautiously at your power's limit.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is realigned but the patient still feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do whatever it takes to put it back in its natural place. Then, moisten a cloth in black styptic wine and cleanly apply it if it's summer time. Do not apply any grease or oil on the wound as it may cause infection. Afterward, administer bandages once you've reset the bone, leaving the wound open. Cut away excess skin around the wound according to its size, taking care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture. Many foolish physicians have done this and caused harm or death to patients due to corruption. Therefore, ensure that the bandage is softer and gentler than usual for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that something bad may happen there, as we have said, and you find pain at that place, then do not apply cauterizing irons; but wrap hard bandages around it instead.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first or second day that the wound is beginning to close, then remove what you have applied with all vinegar, and apply healing ointment to it, such as treacle ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must wash the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is clean and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be bandaged in such a way that the wound drains easily downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it does not heal but the wound keeps opening again, know that there are small bone fragments there, which is why you must scrape the wound with a spoon and remove all these unnecessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula occurs in the place, or another manner of corruption, then you must cure it according to what is said in its chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the thighbone or shoulder blade, and others similar ones of large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death results. Leave it until it rots. By chance it will fall off after 20 or 30 days later, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the sparks that come from the soldering
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often find afterwards the health of the bone broken, especially when it is near the joint, and it is ugly to see the figure of the limb; and by chance the limb cannot perform its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore beware if the bone is fresh: then let the administrator apply medicines that are astringent, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others. Take any of these things or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with axle grease; put them on the bone in compresses, bind it well, and do not remove it for several days. Then remove it, and start again with another one until the swelling is gone. Or you can press upon a piece of polished lead well-made; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the swelling has already turned hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut off the excess. Or have it shaved by some barber until it is removed, and cure it until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break in the bone is healed, and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or because there were too many movements, not at the right time; or because there was little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is: feed the patient and make their body soft until blood increases within them; have them take baths, give them joy and happiness; then apply pitch to the limb so that it attracts great nourishment, and frequently wash it with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and let it return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	When a limb is twisted after healing,
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone breaks open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb again anew, for many foolish physicians have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and sometimes death; yet if the joints and the twisted parts are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or herbs that soften should be cooked, such as fig leaves and roots and melilot and similar things; and make a moistening plaster, such as diacoulion well made, and you take the mucilage of figs, and cook it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster therewith; or you take fat figs, and grind them with fennel seed, and similar medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation occurs from prolonged and continuous friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange gentle movement for the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocations are twisted and hardened like stone, and need to be removed with iron, then one must cut right up to the bone with a sharp scalpel; and take care and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves from its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens to someone, one must promptly reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place becomes inflamed, and perhaps is hardly reset to its proper position; therefore one must not move it while it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains. Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient rest, until the swelling has subsided; then elevate the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as they come into their proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated on both sides, and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their places and softened somewhat; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, so that saliva flows out of the mouth and he cannot hold it in or close his mouth, and speech becomes tangled.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns with several manipulations.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it hastily, without delay; and in such a manner that the attendants hold the head of the patient, and the master places his pouch with one hand on the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is double-sided; and let both hands be ready, to apply pressure evenly; and instruct the patient to soften their jaws, moving them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the master holds it steady until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reset is difficult, even if both jaws are reset together, warm water and oil should be used until they reset easily; do not delay the reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes without softening, then place moistened cloths made of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, with both shoulders between two pillows so that they do not move to the right or left, nor strain themselves when chewing, but eat soft food until the pain subsides and the jaws are healed. Then they may eat what they wish easily, without opening the mouth excessively while eating and drinking, until the jaw is completely healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset accurately within one hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and continuous shivering follow, and possibly abdominal dropsy, and sometimes vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see that, know that it is lost; and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from within its continuity and from the fish (i.e., the hand), but sometimes it dislocates backwards, which can be felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the reduction is as follows: have the patient lie on their back and extend their arms; then press firmly with your palm at its location, and it will return to place. Then apply the splint and bandage, ensuring that the head towards the side does not dislocate again; if it does, reset it back into place as we have described, then reapply the splint and bandage, securing it tightly. Instruct the patient to rest until they are healthy again; similarly, the shoulder blade is reduced when it is dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder can become dislocated: first, it dislocates at the part of the collarbone underneath; second, at the breastbone; and sometimes it dislocates above, which happens rarely. It does not dislocate behind or inside for the nerves, and often dislocates below towards the collarbone, especially those with a lot of flesh, as they quickly become dislocated; those with less flesh hardly ever dislocate and rarely return.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes men suffer an injury or fracture, causing the shoulder to swell with a hot abscess and leading them to believe it is dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must examine it until you are certain; then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocations are recognizable when they occur towards the collarbone. You will find a clear difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one; at the top of the shoulder, you will feel a hollow, and below the collarbone, you will feel the head of the shoulder as if it were an egg. The patient cannot bring their hand to their side or move it in any way. If the dislocation is above, it is not concealed but is easily detectable upon touch. This type of dislocation can only be reset if it is recent or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the servant lifts the hand of the sick person upwards, then places his fingers beneath the shoulder blade, and forces the joint upwards to its place; and the servant lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then places it beneath - so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days after, then the sick person should be bathed in warm water; and the servant should prepare a softening and soothing ointment, such as decoction of mallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and this should be applied. Then the sick person should be placed on their back, and a cloth of even thickness, not too soft or hard, should be placed beneath the shoulder blade; then the physician places his heel on the cloth and gently lifts the head of the shoulder bone, and pulls the hand of the sick person; another servant should hold the head of the sick person so that it does not move downwards. The shoulder returns immediately to its place, and if you wish, reset it according to this manner: and it is necessary that a man who is taller than the sick person be present; he should stand upright next to the ribcage, and put his shoulder beneath the shoulder blade of the sick person, and lift the shoulder upwards so that the sick person hangs from the arm; another servant pulls the hand of the sick person downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the dislocation is also reset in another manner: take a long stick and fix it into the ground so that the head of the shoulder leans on it as on a pillar, but neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, with soft cloths underneath him, and let the patient lie along the length of the wood; then stretch his hand downwards from another side correctly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return despite all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a stick of 2 palms' length and 4 fingers' width, which has a round head for easy entry into the socket deep under the shoulder blade, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place the head of the wood wrapped in cloths on top of the shoulder so that the wood does not burn the patient; then place it under the shoulder blade of the patient; and stretch his arm over the long wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the hand at the elbow, then place the arm over the edge of a wide stool, and let the hand hang downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, however that may be, then you must place beneath the armpit a spherical wad of wool evenly, then put on top of the whole shoulder and around the plaster prepared with flour of millet mixed with incense and egg albumen, then press firmly beneath the armpit, twist the bandage over the plaster, and wrap your hand around its neck.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he should apply poultice sparingly so that the limb is comforted for it will heal faster; then apply more after six or seven days and move it. And if it is firmly closed but not softened, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place due to moisture that has come or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries through three holes as it is set forth in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after seven days the dislocation does not mend, nor can he raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened. And know that the joint will never be set back in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs towards the breastbone, and breasts, or behind is caused by forceful impact and stretching of hands, administered by another person. Treat it until it is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is stiffness in the limb and slowness of movement, then the patient should apply many baths until that stiffness is alleviated and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated towards its front and returns to its front; and if it is dislocated on all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation has not been reduced, for one can see it well and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you align the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is knocked out of place and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before an abscess forms there, for if an abscess forms there, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; thus it is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and sometimes death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you can return it to its place with your two hands; and extend his arm with both of yours; and spread his arms apart, and the hands of the healer around the elbow above and below, and place the joint at his fingertips together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when you bend his hand towards his palm, and press from the root of the palm where the elbow is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and it is necessary that two ministers extend the arm, and two ministers hold it so that it does not move during extension; then twist the arm on each side, then wrap a long and wide cloth around it; and when the healer has joined the joint with his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint forcefully until it returns; and when it is in its place, then put on a dry compress with egg yolk, and bind it tightly, and suspend the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for a few days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie it gently and leave it be; and if you see that the joint is not properly aligned, then recommence the setting and tie it up gently and leave it thus for several days until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if there is great heat after the reduction of the joint and it moves, then bathe it gently and rub it warmly and press until it is soothed; or place on the joint a poultice of fat sheep's wool, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and place it in hot water; and when it sweats, wipe the joint temperately, then replace the poultice and enter into the bath; and thus do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see fit, then place on fresh moist fern heated with butter and hold it on; then it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	If the joint of the hand is dislocated and its reduction is easy, then it must be reset quickly in the same position where it was dislocated, before the place becomes swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is performed thus: place the injured hand on a table, extend the fingers of the patient, and gently place your own palm over the joint's prominence. Push firmly until it returns to its normal position. Always ensure that it is properly reduced in place. Then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's palm on the table and gently press your own hand onto the prominence of that joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it goes back now, then all is well. But if not, apply warm compresses to relieve inflammation and prevent the dislocation from recurring again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and does no harm to the patient except that his hand is weakened, and he can grasp nothing entirely: know then that the nerve or artery is severed; there is no other means of healing except by cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else would help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the bandage that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then untie it and let it remain thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then apply warm water compresses, and rub it until it is smooth.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated at each joint, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the belly; therefore, reduce the dislocation until it returns to its place, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, then straighten it that day; and tie it as we have said, and untie it on the third day, and move it, and tie it again tightly; do this often until it is stable. Do the same if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do so until it is healed.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the hip bone of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip bone of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are many dislocations, then there is no remedy, for the person hastens the patient's death.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the evacuations come forth without control, and cannot be held back, and many times some member becomes softened, either both thighs or both arms or one; And often the hip bone moves in four parts; that which moves at the rear is called 'gilbositez': but there is no remedy or healing for it all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or blow or similar things, the ancient ones had ways of cure with great words, but there is not always great benefit in them; but I have shortened it according to my intention and made tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling which comes to the breast in front, none has health; and likewise that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot cure it but oneself who knows properly how to deal with it when it comes to the back, as I say. And let the patient be stretched out on their face in a flat place, and have something firm underneath them so they do not bruise themselves; then stick one stake at the head firmly into the ground, and another at the feet, and tie one rope beneath the elbows of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know how to hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and let them be held firmly, as we have said, and the physician place his palms on the spine firmly until it moves.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not move with this treatment, then take a board of three feet in length and place it under the patient, and let the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the spine, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it moves back into place. And if you see, do this to the one that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the invalid's arm, one on each side, and at a distance of a palm's length between them; and let there be a hole in each stake where the cord will turn, and let the stakes be firmly fixed in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of stakes, place a turning stake on which the cord will turn, with two smaller stakes of a palm's length to turn the turning stake; then tie the cord that is among the stakes at the head to one turning stake, and the other cord at the foot to the other turning stake, and each minister shall turn his turning stake on all the cord, and the master shall place the bandage evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then place a dried plaster with abundant eggs upon it, and then the poultice, and then the bandage of a tablet three fingers wide, which shall cover the place of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a cord as we have said, and let the patient use gentle nourishment until they are healed; and if any complication arises at the end of the healing process, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines along with the bandage that we have mentioned before; and sometimes one should apply a piece of lead, and sometimes the swelling appears on the back spine, and it is thought to be dislocation; but this is the bone that protrudes, therefore one must not be presumptuous: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and shoulder dislocation occurs alone, not as with other joints. The joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: within and without, and front and back; and more especially within others, and rarely before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of its dislocation within is that when one joins the lame leg with the sound one, it appears longer and the lame knee opens more widely than the sound one. The lame cannot bend his knee at the fire; and the place near which there is swelling from an abscess is hot because the head of the thigh has moved there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which moves without is that these accidents are opposite to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of that which happens in front is that the leg seems well-formed; nevertheless, it does not bend at the knee without pain. If one wants to make it go forward, it cannot do so, and it retains its urine. The ankle swells, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one to whom it happens behind is that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in its place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this type of dislocation is that if the dislocation is ancient and remains in its position, there is no need for treatment; and it should not be approached with presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for one whose dislocation is fresh and there are four types of dislocation, you should quickly return the joint to its place, extend it outward and inward, move it to the right and left. Perhaps it will return to its original position and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong minister and extend the leg strongly with both hands or tie one of them on the knee; and another minister should place his hand above in such a way that he places his hands under his buttocks, then gently pull up on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and all stretch simultaneously upward and downward until the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar joints. If the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat its counterpart. When the dislocation is at the hip joint, you should lay the patient on their sound side, place a rope under the root of the thigh and below the angle of the pelvis, then stretch the rope upwards towards the angle and the gluteal region; then have some assistants take his arms and embrace the larger bone of the thigh, extending it forcefully: now it will return to its proper place. This manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have described, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a soft, strong rope on both heels and knees, keeping the injured leg stretched out about two spans more than the other; then hang him from the top of a pole, with his arms hanging down about two spans off the ground. Then command one assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, while another hangs from the patient, forcefully embracing the thigh as the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the hip, let the patient lie down as we have said in the case of those with kyphoscoliosis; and apply traction to the ligaments above the injured leg properly, and also above the foot. Then place two sticks: one at the head and one at the feet. Then insert one stick between the thighs of the patient in this manner. And have moist bandages ready around it so that the patient does not blister. Then each attendant extends towards him, and the physician places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, then place him on a board and press down as we have said in the case of kyphoscoliosis, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is anterior, then extend the injured leg promptly, and as I have said; and let the physician place his knee on the angle of the injured leg, then press with his other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	**And if the dislocation is at the hip,** do not extend the patient downwards nor raise them onto the ground, but they should be placed as if their hip were dislocated at the back, as we have said concerning childbirth on the two hips; and they should lie on their face, with the sheet extended as we have previously stated, and one must press upon the joint with a table; it will be set when the patient extends their legs, and they are even. Then join the thighs together, place the splint, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move. Let them rest for three or four days, then untie it, and replace the splint. If you see that they are even, then bind again as before and let them rest for three days. Then untie it, and make them walk gently until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	**Regarding dislocation of the knee,**
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign of this is that you should tell the patient to bend their leg towards their hip, and if it does not move smoothly, know that they are dislocated. And the treatment for all these is that you make the patient sit upright, extend their leg as much as possible, place your back against their thigh, and put their foot on yours; then grasp their knee with both hands and draw it towards your belly, then strongly press both sides of the knee joint inward; and another assistant extends their foot until the knee returns to its proper position, and the sign is that they can easily move their leg smoothly at the hip. Then place a bandage over it, make them keep the leg against the hip, and bind them tightly for three or four days, then release them. And the patient should not walk until the limb has healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly aligned, then strongly extend it, as we have said in the treatment of hip dislocation, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	And of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes twisted and sometimes fully dislocated both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle swells, and tends forward towards the part where it is dislocated; the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only twisted.
