Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright, and pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then left hand twice, stretch it upwards, and place the foot gently upwards; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it does not return, repeat the procedure, as it may return. If it still cannot be reduced in this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, firmly plant a pole in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around to prevent injury to the patient; then one attendant holds the thigh, and another extends the foot with their hands or using a loop tied onto the heel; then both extend equally, and the pole should always be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient steady when stretching it; then the physician gently reduces the dislocation with their hands, and another attendant holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, then apply the plaster and bandages tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature loosens, then tighten it; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before this time, it is not certain that they will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil happens to appear, then you must calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	Of the eyes
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the eyes are dislocated, they should be gently extended without effort; this is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot, then you should have the patient sit on a level place or on a table completely upright, and put your foot on what opens from those joints, then press on your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is even and nothing opens there, then put under the sole of the foot a two-legged table, then bind it tightly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to reset it, often the patient dies: therefore be not presumptuous in treatment unless you are skilled in the art and have practiced it long, and are pitiful and merciful and cautious, not hasty; and at first use things that cool inflammation hot, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place before the inflamed swelling comes on; and when the limb is in place, then apply things that cool inflammation hot, and treat the wound with drying ointments as it should be done; and if with dislocation there is fracture, and small bones dislocated, set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into fear's path, according to what I have said, for this avails you more according to your Creator, and for the sake of your weapon and body.
Amen	May it be so.
